فصل الأمر بالشيء يدل على حسن المأمور به

ثم المأمور به في حق الحسن نوعان: حسن بنفسه وحسن لغيره، فالحسن بنفسه مثل: الإيمان بالله تعالى وشكر المنعم والصدق والعدل والصلاة ونحوها من العبادات الخالصة، فحكم هذا النوع أنه إذا وجب على العبد أداؤه لا يسقط إلا بالأداء وهذا فيما لا يحتمل السقوط مثل: الإيمان بالله تعالى، وأما ما يحتمل السقوط فهو يسقط بالأداء أو بإسقاط الآمر كسقوط الزكاة بهلاك النصاب. وعلى هذا قلنا: إذا وجبت الصلاة في أول الوقت سقط الواجب بالأداء أو بإسقاط الشارع كإسقاط الصلاة بالحيض والنفاس والجنون والإغماء إلى ست صلوات بخلاف النوم ولو بقدر الست، باعتراض الجنون والحيض والنفاس في آخر الوقت باعتبار أن الشرع أسقطها، بالعقل وهو فاسد؛ لأن العقل لا مدخل له في إيجاب الشيء؛ إذ الواجب ما يثاب المرء بفعله ويعاقب بتركه، والعقل لا يدرك أن هذا الشيء مما يثاب بفعله ويعاقب بتركه؛ لأن هذا حكم شرعي لا عقلي فلا يكون العقل موجباً، ولأنه يجوز ورود النسخ على حسن المأمور به ولو كان حسنها بعقل لما جاز حسن العقل لا يرد عليه النسخ كحسن شكر المنعم والعدل والإحسان، كذا في "المعدن".

(۱) قوله: [في حق الحسن] أي: في ذات الحسن، وأما في كيفية الحسن فأربعة أنواع؛ لأن الحسن بنفسه نوعان: حسن لا يحتمل السقوط وحسن يحتمله وكذا الحسن لغيره نوعان: ما يحصل ذلك بفعل المأمور به، وما يحصل بفعل مقصود، كذا في "المعدن".

(۲) قوله [والصلاة] أي الصلاة حسن في نفسها؛ لأنها من أولها إلى آخرها تعظيم للرب تعالى بالأقوال والأفعال وثناء عليه وخشوع له وقيام بين يديه وجلسة لحضوره، وإن كانت الكميات وتعداد الركعات والأوقات والشرائط لا يستقل بمعرفتها العقل فكان محتاجاً إلى الشريعة الغراء.

(۳) قوله: [مثل الإيمان] والمراد بالإيمان هاهنا التصديق فإنه ركن أصلي لا يحتمل السقوط بحال بخلاف الإقرار فإنه ركن إما زائد أو شرط إجراء الأحكام في الدنيا على حسب الاختلاف بين العلماء، فإنه يسقط بقدر الإكراه، كذا في "المعدن".

(٤) قوله : [في أول الوقت] فيه إشارة إلى أن نفس الوجوب يثبت بأول جزء من الوقت وجوباً موسعاً عند المصنف، كما هو المذهب الصحيح.

ثم قال: حتى يجب القضاء إذا فات. وكالإكراه على ترك الصلاة. عنه عند هذه العوارض ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت وعدم الماء واللباس ونحوه، أي الواجب. من المأمور به. حتى يجب عليه التيمم. كما في اشتباه القبلة النوع الثاني ما يكون حسنا بواسطة الغير وذلك مثل: السعي إلى الجمعة مأمور به بقوله تعالى فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله الخ. والوضوء للصلاة، فإن السعي حسن بواسطة كونه مفضيا إلى أداء الجمعة لا في نفسه. والوضوء حسن بواسطة كونه مفتاحا للصلاة، وحكم هذا النوع أنه يسقط بعد الوجوب بسقوط تلك الواسطة، حتى أن السعي لا يجب على من لا جمعة عليه ولا يجب الوضوء على من لا صلاة عليه، ولو سعى إلى الجمعة فحمل مكرها إلى موضع آخر قبل إقامة الجمعة يجب عليه السعي ثانيا، ولو كان معتكفا في المسجد الجامع يكون السعي ساقطا عنه وكذلك لو توضأ فأحدث قبل أداء الصلاة عليه الوضوء ثانيا، ولو كان متوضئا عند وجوب الصلاة لا يجب عليه تجديد الوضوء، والقريب من ...

(۱) قوله: [ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت] بتفريطه فيأثم أو بغير تفريطه فلا يأثم، وعلى كل تقدير، يجب القضاء و في عدم الماء يجب التيمم أي الصلاة به، وفي عدم اللباس تجب عرياناً ولا تسقط في حين من الأحيان، فعلم أن مطلق العوارض غير مسقط للوجوب بل بعضها الذي اعتبره الشارع في باب الحرج والضرورة البالغة إلى حد معتبر عند الشرع مسقط للوجوب فافهم، كذا في "المعدن".

(۲) قوله: [واللباس] حتى خير بين أن يصلي قائماً ويتم الركوع والسجود وبين أن يصلي قاعداً ويؤديهما بالإيماء.

(۳) قوله: [والوضوء... إلخ] فإن الوضوء تبريد وتنظيف الأعضاء وإضاعة الماء، وذلك ليس بحسن في ذاته؛ إذ ليس فيه معنى العبادة إنما حسن لأجل أداء الصلاة.

(٤) قوله: [والقريب] وفيه كلام، وهو أن قريب الشيء يلزم أن يكون غيره فيلزم أن يكون الحدود ونحوها حسناً لعينه؛ إذ لا واسطة بين الحسن لغيره وبين الحسن لعينه فإذا كان قريباً لما هو حسن لغيره يلزم أن يكون غيره، وغيره ليس إلا الحسن لعينه بناءً على انتفاء الواسطة، وكون الحدود وأمثالها من الحسن [؟]
Chapter: The command over a thing indicates the goodness of the commanded thing. Then the commanded thing in respect of goodness is of two types: good in itself and good by virtue of something else. Good in itself is like faith in Allah the Exalted, gratitude to the Benefactor, truthfulness, justice, prayer and similar purely devotional acts. The ruling of this type is that when it becomes obligatory upon the servant to perform it, it is not dropped except by performance—this in what does not admit of being dropped, like faith in Allah the Exalted. As for what admits of being dropped, it is dropped by performance or by the commander's dropping it, like the dropping of zakah by the destruction of the nisab. Based on this we said: when prayer becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time, the obligation is dropped by performance or by the Lawgiver's dropping it, such as dropping prayer due to menstruation, post-natal bleeding, insanity, and unconsciousness up to six prayers—contrary to sleep even if equal to six—by the occurrence of insanity, menstruation, post-natal bleeding at the end of the time, considering that the Lawgiver dropped them. By reason—and it is invalid—because reason has no role in making a thing obligatory; for the obligatory is that which one is rewarded for doing and punished for leaving, and reason does not perceive that this thing is such that one is rewarded for doing it and punished for leaving it, because this is a legal ruling, not rational. So reason cannot be a cause of obligation. And because abrogation is possible concerning the goodness of the commanded thing; if its goodness were by reason, abrogation would not be permissible, for rational goodness is not subject to abrogation, like the goodness of gratitude to the Benefactor, justice, and benevolence. Thus in al-Ma'din. (1) His statement: [in respect of goodness] i.e., in the essence of goodness. As for the modality of goodness, there are four types: good in itself is of two types: good that does not admit of being dropped and good that admits it; similarly good by virtue of something else is of two types: that which is attained by the commanded act itself, and that which is attained by an intended act. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) His statement: [and prayer] i.e., prayer is good in itself because from beginning to end it is glorification of the Lord Almighty with words and actions, praise of Him, humility before Him, standing before Him, and sitting for His presence; even though the quantities, number of rak'ahs, times, and conditions cannot be independently known by reason, so it is in need of the noble Sharia. (3) His statement: [like faith] - what is meant by faith here is affirmation (tasdiq), for it is the essential pillar that does not admit of being dropped under any circumstance, unlike confession (iqrar) which is either an additional pillar or a condition for implementing legal rulings in this world according to scholarly difference; indeed it is dropped to the extent of coercion. Thus in al-Ma'din. (4) His statement: [at the beginning of the time] - it indicates that the obligation itself is established at the first part of the time as an extended obligation according to the author, as is the correct school. Then he said: so that the making-up is obligatory if it is missed. And like coercion to abandon prayer. It is not dropped due to narrowness of time, lack of water, clothing, and the like, i.e., the obligation from the commanded thing, so that tayammum becomes obligatory. As in the case of uncertainty about the qibla. The second type is that which is good by virtue of something else, such as walking to Friday prayer, commanded by His statement: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah,' etc., and ablution for prayer. For walking is good by virtue of leading to the performance of Friday prayer, not in itself. And ablution is good by virtue of being a key to prayer. The ruling of this type is that it is dropped after obligation by the dropping of that intermediary, such that walking is not obligatory upon one who is not required to attend Friday prayer, and ablution is not obligatory upon one who is not required to pray. If one walked to Friday prayer and was carried involuntarily to another place before the establishment of Friday prayer, he must walk again. If one was in seclusion (i'tikaf) in the congregational mosque, walking is dropped for him. Similarly, if one performed ablution and then had an event before performing prayer, he must perform ablution again. If one was already in a state of ablution at the time prayer became obligatory, he does not have to renew ablution. And that which is close to... (1) His statement: [and it is not dropped due to narrowness of time] - if due to his negligence, he sins; if without negligence, he does not sin. In either case, making up is obligatory. In the absence of water, tayammum is obligatory, i.e., prayer with it. In the absence of clothing, prayer is obligatory naked, and it is not dropped at any time. So it is understood that absolute impediments do not drop the obligation; rather, only those that the Lawgiver has considered in the chapter of hardship and dire necessity to a limit considered by the Law are dropping of obligation. Understand. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) His statement: [and clothing] - even he is given the choice between praying standing while performing bowing and prostration fully, or praying sitting while performing them by gesture. (3) His statement: [and ablution...] - indeed ablution is cooling and cleaning of limbs and wasting water, and that is not good in itself, for there is no meaning of worship in it; rather it is good only for the sake of performing prayer. (4) His statement: [and that which is close] - there is discussion about it: that the close of something necessarily must be other than it, so it would follow that penalties (hudud) and the like are good in themselves, because there is no intermediary between good by virtue of something else and good in itself. If something is close to what is good by virtue of something else, it must be other than it, and other than it is nothing but good in itself based on the negation of an intermediary. And that penalties and the like are of the good... [cut off]
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Fiqh establishes a foundational rule: when the Lawgiver (Allah or His Messenger) commands something, that very command indicates that the commanded act is good (hasan). The word 'hasan' here carries a legal/ethical meaning: it is something commendable in the sight of the Lawgiver. The passage then refines this by distinguishing two categories of goodness in the commanded act: intrinsic goodness (hasan bi-nafsihi) and acquired goodness (hasan li-ghayrihi). The author first addresses intrinsic goodness: acts whose goodness is inherent, such as faith (iman), gratitude, truthfulness, justice, and purely devotional acts like prayer. These are good in themselves regardless of external factors. The ruling for such acts is that once they become obligatory, they are not dropped except by actual performance—except in cases where the obligation itself admits of being dropped, like zakah when the wealth is destroyed. Prayer, however, is intrinsic in its essence, though its specific details (times, rak'ahs) are revealed. The passage then argues against the rationalist view (attributed to the Mu'tazila) that reason alone can determine obligation and goodness. The Hanafi position is that obligation is a legal matter; reason cannot independently know reward and punishment. Furthermore, if goodness were purely rational, abrogation would be impossible, whereas divine commands are subject to abrogation. The second category is goodness by virtue of something else: acts that are not good in themselves but become good as means to a praiseworthy end. Examples: walking to Friday prayer and performing ablution for prayer. Their goodness derives from the intended act (Friday prayer, obligatory prayer). Consequently, if the intermediary falls away (e.g., no Friday prayer obligation), the commanded act (walking) is no longer required. The commentary (hashiya) expands on subtle points: the fourfold division of hasan, the nature of prayer, the definition of iman as affirmation, and the technical details of when the obligation of prayer is established. The passage closes with rulings on situations of duress and on the issue of acts that are 'close' to being good by virtue of something else, raising a nuanced discussion about hudud penalties.

Key Terms
الحسن بنفسه (al-ḥasan bi-nafsihi): Goodness that inheres in the act itself, such as iman and prayer; it is not derived from an external purpose.
الحسن لغيره (al-ḥasan li-ghayrihi): Goodness acquired from the act's leading to a praiseworthy end, like ablution for prayer.
المأمور به (al-ma'mūr bihī): The act commanded by the Lawgiver; its goodness is implied by the command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling for an act that is hasan li-ghayrihi after the intermediary (the higher purpose) drops?
A) It remains obligatory until performed.
B) It becomes non-obligatory because its reason has ceased.
C) It becomes a recommended act (mandub).
D) It is dropped only if explicitly abrogated by the Lawgiver.

Key Takeaway
Acts commanded by Allah are good, but goodness is either intrinsic (obligation remains until performed or explicitly dropped) or acquired (obligation drops with the end that justified it).

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Refuting the Rationalist View: Reason Cannot Determine Obligation
Refuting the rationalist view that reason determines obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi proof that reason cannot independently know legal obligation and explain why the possibility of abrogation undermines the rationalist view.

Core Idea
Reason cannot make something obligatory; obligation is a legal ruling known only through revelation.

The passage not only classifies goodness but also refutes the claim that reason alone can determine the goodness and obligation of acts. The Hanafi school insists that obligation (wujub) is a shar'i matter, not rational. This lesson unpacks the argument: the definition of wajib involves reward and punishment, which are not known by reason, and commanded acts can be abrogated, showing their goodness is not eternal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rationalist claim
The rationalist (Mu'tazilite) claim is that reason can independently determine the goodness of acts, and thus can make them obligatory. The text refutes this specifically regarding acts like gratitude to the Benefactor (shukr al-mun'im).
2
State the first Hanafi proof: definition of wajib
The wajib is defined as 'that which one is rewarded for doing and punished for leaving'. This is a legal (shar'i) classification; reason cannot perceive reward and punishment, which are known only through revelation. Hence, reason cannot be a source of obligation.
Text: 'الواجب ما يثاب المرء بفعله ويعاقب بتركه، والعقل لا يدرك أن هذا الشيء مما يثاب بفعله ويعاقب بتركه'.
3
State the second Hanafi proof: possibility of abrogation
If the goodness of an act were determined by reason, it would be eternal and unchangeable, as rational truths are. However, divine commands are subject to abrogation (naskh), which means their goodness is not eternal, thus not purely rational.
Text: 'يجوز ورود النسخ على حسن المأمور به ولو كان حسنها بعقل لما جاز'.
4
Apply the proofs to a concrete example: gratitude to the Benefactor
Even though reason considers shukr al-mun'im good, the Hanafis argue that legal obligation does not follow. The goodness is rational but the obligation is purely from revelation. The fact that the Sharia could abrogate the command to express gratitude shows its goodness is not rational in the sense that it cannot be changed.

Source Text

فصل الأمر بالشيء يدل على حسن المأمور به

ثم المأمور به في حق الحسن نوعان: حسن بنفسه وحسن لغيره، فالحسن بنفسه مثل: الإيمان بالله تعالى وشكر المنعم والصدق والعدل والصلاة ونحوها من العبادات الخالصة، فحكم هذا النوع أنه إذا وجب على العبد أداؤه لا يسقط إلا بالأداء وهذا فيما لا يحتمل السقوط مثل: الإيمان بالله تعالى، وأما ما يحتمل السقوط فهو يسقط بالأداء أو بإسقاط الآمر كسقوط الزكاة بهلاك النصاب. وعلى هذا قلنا: إذا وجبت الصلاة في أول الوقت سقط الواجب بالأداء أو بإسقاط الشارع كإسقاط الصلاة بالحيض والنفاس والجنون والإغماء إلى ست صلوات بخلاف النوم ولو بقدر الست، باعتراض الجنون والحيض والنفاس في آخر الوقت باعتبار أن الشرع أسقطها، بالعقل وهو فاسد؛ لأن العقل لا مدخل له في إيجاب الشيء؛ إذ الواجب ما يثاب المرء بفعله ويعاقب بتركه، والعقل لا يدرك أن هذا الشيء مما يثاب بفعله ويعاقب بتركه؛ لأن هذا حكم شرعي لا عقلي فلا يكون العقل موجباً، ولأنه يجوز ورود النسخ على حسن المأمور به ولو كان حسنها بعقل لما جاز حسن العقل لا يرد عليه النسخ كحسن شكر المنعم والعدل والإحسان، كذا في "المعدن".

(۱) قوله: [في حق الحسن] أي: في ذات الحسن، وأما في كيفية الحسن فأربعة أنواع؛ لأن الحسن بنفسه نوعان: حسن لا يحتمل السقوط وحسن يحتمله وكذا الحسن لغيره نوعان: ما يحصل ذلك بفعل المأمور به، وما يحصل بفعل مقصود، كذا في "المعدن".

(۲) قوله [والصلاة] أي الصلاة حسن في نفسها؛ لأنها من أولها إلى آخرها تعظيم للرب تعالى بالأقوال والأفعال وثناء عليه وخشوع له وقيام بين يديه وجلسة لحضوره، وإن كانت الكميات وتعداد الركعات والأوقات والشرائط لا يستقل بمعرفتها العقل فكان محتاجاً إلى الشريعة الغراء.

(۳) قوله: [مثل الإيمان] والمراد بالإيمان هاهنا التصديق فإنه ركن أصلي لا يحتمل السقوط بحال بخلاف الإقرار فإنه ركن إما زائد أو شرط إجراء الأحكام في الدنيا على حسب الاختلاف بين العلماء، فإنه يسقط بقدر الإكراه، كذا في "المعدن".

(٤) قوله : [في أول الوقت] فيه إشارة إلى أن نفس الوجوب يثبت بأول جزء من الوقت وجوباً موسعاً عند المصنف، كما هو المذهب الصحيح.

ثم قال: حتى يجب القضاء إذا فات. وكالإكراه على ترك الصلاة. عنه عند هذه العوارض ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت وعدم الماء واللباس ونحوه، أي الواجب. من المأمور به. حتى يجب عليه التيمم. كما في اشتباه القبلة النوع الثاني ما يكون حسنا بواسطة الغير وذلك مثل: السعي إلى الجمعة مأمور به بقوله تعالى فاسعوا إلى ذكر الله الخ. والوضوء للصلاة، فإن السعي حسن بواسطة كونه مفضيا إلى أداء الجمعة لا في نفسه. والوضوء حسن بواسطة كونه مفتاحا للصلاة، وحكم هذا النوع أنه يسقط بعد الوجوب بسقوط تلك الواسطة، حتى أن السعي لا يجب على من لا جمعة عليه ولا يجب الوضوء على من لا صلاة عليه، ولو سعى إلى الجمعة فحمل مكرها إلى موضع آخر قبل إقامة الجمعة يجب عليه السعي ثانيا، ولو كان معتكفا في المسجد الجامع يكون السعي ساقطا عنه وكذلك لو توضأ فأحدث قبل أداء الصلاة عليه الوضوء ثانيا، ولو كان متوضئا عند وجوب الصلاة لا يجب عليه تجديد الوضوء، والقريب من ...

(۱) قوله: [ولا يسقط بضيق الوقت] بتفريطه فيأثم أو بغير تفريطه فلا يأثم، وعلى كل تقدير، يجب القضاء و في عدم الماء يجب التيمم أي الصلاة به، وفي عدم اللباس تجب عرياناً ولا تسقط في حين من الأحيان، فعلم أن مطلق العوارض غير مسقط للوجوب بل بعضها الذي اعتبره الشارع في باب الحرج والضرورة البالغة إلى حد معتبر عند الشرع مسقط للوجوب فافهم، كذا في "المعدن".

(۲) قوله: [واللباس] حتى خير بين أن يصلي قائماً ويتم الركوع والسجود وبين أن يصلي قاعداً ويؤديهما بالإيماء.

(۳) قوله: [والوضوء... إلخ] فإن الوضوء تبريد وتنظيف الأعضاء وإضاعة الماء، وذلك ليس بحسن في ذاته؛ إذ ليس فيه معنى العبادة إنما حسن لأجل أداء الصلاة.

(٤) قوله: [والقريب] وفيه كلام، وهو أن قريب الشيء يلزم أن يكون غيره فيلزم أن يكون الحدود ونحوها حسناً لعينه؛ إذ لا واسطة بين الحسن لغيره وبين الحسن لعينه فإذا كان قريباً لما هو حسن لغيره يلزم أن يكون غيره، وغيره ليس إلا الحسن لعينه بناءً على انتفاء الواسطة، وكون الحدود وأمثالها من الحسن [؟]
Chapter: The command over a thing indicates the goodness of the commanded thing. Then the commanded thing in respect of goodness is of two types: good in itself and good by virtue of something else. Good in itself is like faith in Allah the Exalted, gratitude to the Benefactor, truthfulness, justice, prayer and similar purely devotional acts. The ruling of this type is that when it becomes obligatory upon the servant to perform it, it is not dropped except by performance—this in what does not admit of being dropped, like faith in Allah the Exalted. As for what admits of being dropped, it is dropped by performance or by the commander's dropping it, like the dropping of zakah by the destruction of the nisab. Based on this we said: when prayer becomes obligatory at the beginning of the time, the obligation is dropped by performance or by the Lawgiver's dropping it, such as dropping prayer due to menstruation, post-natal bleeding, insanity, and unconsciousness up to six prayers—contrary to sleep even if equal to six—by the occurrence of insanity, menstruation, post-natal bleeding at the end of the time, considering that the Lawgiver dropped them. By reason—and it is invalid—because reason has no role in making a thing obligatory; for the obligatory is that which one is rewarded for doing and punished for leaving, and reason does not perceive that this thing is such that one is rewarded for doing it and punished for leaving it, because this is a legal ruling, not rational. So reason cannot be a cause of obligation. And because abrogation is possible concerning the goodness of the commanded thing; if its goodness were by reason, abrogation would not be permissible, for rational goodness is not subject to abrogation, like the goodness of gratitude to the Benefactor, justice, and benevolence. Thus in al-Ma'din. (1) His statement: [in respect of goodness] i.e., in the essence of goodness. As for the modality of goodness, there are four types: good in itself is of two types: good that does not admit of being dropped and good that admits it; similarly good by virtue of something else is of two types: that which is attained by the commanded act itself, and that which is attained by an intended act. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) His statement: [and prayer] i.e., prayer is good in itself because from beginning to end it is glorification of the Lord Almighty with words and actions, praise of Him, humility before Him, standing before Him, and sitting for His presence; even though the quantities, number of rak'ahs, times, and conditions cannot be independently known by reason, so it is in need of the noble Sharia. (3) His statement: [like faith] - what is meant by faith here is affirmation (tasdiq), for it is the essential pillar that does not admit of being dropped under any circumstance, unlike confession (iqrar) which is either an additional pillar or a condition for implementing legal rulings in this world according to scholarly difference; indeed it is dropped to the extent of coercion. Thus in al-Ma'din. (4) His statement: [at the beginning of the time] - it indicates that the obligation itself is established at the first part of the time as an extended obligation according to the author, as is the correct school. Then he said: so that the making-up is obligatory if it is missed. And like coercion to abandon prayer. It is not dropped due to narrowness of time, lack of water, clothing, and the like, i.e., the obligation from the commanded thing, so that tayammum becomes obligatory. As in the case of uncertainty about the qibla. The second type is that which is good by virtue of something else, such as walking to Friday prayer, commanded by His statement: 'So hasten to the remembrance of Allah,' etc., and ablution for prayer. For walking is good by virtue of leading to the performance of Friday prayer, not in itself. And ablution is good by virtue of being a key to prayer. The ruling of this type is that it is dropped after obligation by the dropping of that intermediary, such that walking is not obligatory upon one who is not required to attend Friday prayer, and ablution is not obligatory upon one who is not required to pray. If one walked to Friday prayer and was carried involuntarily to another place before the establishment of Friday prayer, he must walk again. If one was in seclusion (i'tikaf) in the congregational mosque, walking is dropped for him. Similarly, if one performed ablution and then had an event before performing prayer, he must perform ablution again. If one was already in a state of ablution at the time prayer became obligatory, he does not have to renew ablution. And that which is close to... (1) His statement: [and it is not dropped due to narrowness of time] - if due to his negligence, he sins; if without negligence, he does not sin. In either case, making up is obligatory. In the absence of water, tayammum is obligatory, i.e., prayer with it. In the absence of clothing, prayer is obligatory naked, and it is not dropped at any time. So it is understood that absolute impediments do not drop the obligation; rather, only those that the Lawgiver has considered in the chapter of hardship and dire necessity to a limit considered by the Law are dropping of obligation. Understand. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) His statement: [and clothing] - even he is given the choice between praying standing while performing bowing and prostration fully, or praying sitting while performing them by gesture. (3) His statement: [and ablution...] - indeed ablution is cooling and cleaning of limbs and wasting water, and that is not good in itself, for there is no meaning of worship in it; rather it is good only for the sake of performing prayer. (4) His statement: [and that which is close] - there is discussion about it: that the close of something necessarily must be other than it, so it would follow that penalties (hudud) and the like are good in themselves, because there is no intermediary between good by virtue of something else and good in itself. If something is close to what is good by virtue of something else, it must be other than it, and other than it is nothing but good in itself based on the negation of an intermediary. And that penalties and the like are of the good... [cut off]
Source pages p. 112

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Fiqh establishes a foundational rule: when the Lawgiver (Allah or His Messenger) commands something, that very command indicates that the commanded act is good (hasan). The word 'hasan' here carries a legal/ethical meaning: it is something commendable in the sight of the Lawgiver. The passage then refines this by distinguishing two categories of goodness in the commanded act: intrinsic goodness (hasan bi-nafsihi) and acquired goodness (hasan li-ghayrihi). The author first addresses intrinsic goodness: acts whose goodness is inherent, such as faith (iman), gratitude, truthfulness, justice, and purely devotional acts like prayer. These are good in themselves regardless of external factors. The ruling for such acts is that once they become obligatory, they are not dropped except by actual performance—except in cases where the obligation itself admits of being dropped, like zakah when the wealth is destroyed. Prayer, however, is intrinsic in its essence, though its specific details (times, rak'ahs) are revealed. The passage then argues against the rationalist view (attributed to the Mu'tazila) that reason alone can determine obligation and goodness. The Hanafi position is that obligation is a legal matter; reason cannot independently know reward and punishment. Furthermore, if goodness were purely rational, abrogation would be impossible, whereas divine commands are subject to abrogation. The second category is goodness by virtue of something else: acts that are not good in themselves but become good as means to a praiseworthy end. Examples: walking to Friday prayer and performing ablution for prayer. Their goodness derives from the intended act (Friday prayer, obligatory prayer). Consequently, if the intermediary falls away (e.g., no Friday prayer obligation), the commanded act (walking) is no longer required. The commentary (hashiya) expands on subtle points: the fourfold division of hasan, the nature of prayer, the definition of iman as affirmation, and the technical details of when the obligation of prayer is established. The passage closes with rulings on situations of duress and on the issue of acts that are 'close' to being good by virtue of something else, raising a nuanced discussion about hudud penalties.

Key Terms
الحسن بنفسه (al-ḥasan bi-nafsihi): Goodness that inheres in the act itself, such as iman and prayer; it is not derived from an external purpose.
الحسن لغيره (al-ḥasan li-ghayrihi): Goodness acquired from the act's leading to a praiseworthy end, like ablution for prayer.
المأمور به (al-ma'mūr bihī): The act commanded by the Lawgiver; its goodness is implied by the command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in the passage, why cannot reason be a cause of obligation (wujub)?
A) Because reason is often wrong and unreliable.
B) Because the definition of wajib involves reward and punishment, which are not rationally known.
C) Because all commanded acts are hasan bi-nafsihi, and reason can only know hasan li-ghayrihi.
D) Because reason can only know what is good, not what is obligatory.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, reason can perceive goodness but not create legal obligation; obligation is a Shar'i matter requiring revelation.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

The Command Indicates Goodness: Intrinsic vs. Extrinsic Goodness
Explanation of a usul principle and its application to punishments and jihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi usul principle that a command (amr) indicates the moral goodness (husn) of the commanded act, and differentiate between intrinsic goodness (ḥasan li-ʿaynihi) and extrinsic goodness (ḥasan li-ghayrihi) using the examples of ḥudūd, qiṣāṣ, and jihād.

Core Idea
A command signals the act is good, but that goodness may stem from its consequences, not its essence.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi establishes a foundational rule: when the Lawgiver commands an action, that action is legally considered good (ḥasan). However, the text immediately qualifies this by explaining that many commanded acts are good not in themselves but for the effects they produce—such as deterring crime or repelling evil. Understanding this distinction is essential for proper legal reasoning, as it helps us categorize actions and recognize the rationale behind divine commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Principle
The passage opens with a clear statement: 'al-amr bi al-shay' yadullu 'ala husn al-ma'mur bih' (the command to do something indicates the goodness of the commanded thing). This is the core usul rule we will analyze.
Remember: this principle is general; the rest of the passage provides clarifications and examples.
2
Recognize the Two Types of Goodness
The commentary distinguishes between ḥasan li-ʿaynihi (good in itself) and ḥasan li-ghayrihi (good for another reason). The principle applies to both, but the text focuses on acts that are good extrinsically.
An act like prayer is good in itself; an act like ḥadd is good for its deterrent effect.
3
Examine the Three Examples: Ḥudūd, Qiṣāṣ, Jihād
The text gives three examples of commanded acts that are good extrinsically. Ḥudūd (fixed punishments) are good because they deter crime (e.g., zina, drinking wine). Qiṣāṣ (retaliation) deters murder. Jihād involves destruction but is good for repelling evil and elevating the word of truth. A ḥadīth is cited to show jihād is not good in itself: 'The human is the building of the Lord; cursed is he who destroys it.'
Focus on the rationale: the 'intermediate cause' (crime, aggression) makes the act good.
4
Distinguish from Acts Like Saʿy and Wuḍūʾ
The text contrasts these three with acts like saʿy (running between Safa and Marwah) and wuḍūʾ (ablution), which are also ḥasan li-ghayrihi. However, for saʿy and wuḍūʾ, the extrinsic goal (Friday prayer, prayer) is not achieved by the act itself but by separate actions. For ḥudūd, qiṣāṣ, and jihād, the very act accomplishes the goal (deterrence, elevation).
This distinction shows that even among extrinsically good acts, there are two subcategories: means that directly achieve the end and means that merely prepare for it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الزجر عن وهو أصل المقصود من شرعية. ١٢ كالزنا وشرب الخمر. ١٢ کافر. ۱۲ الجناية، والجهاد حسن بواسطة دفع شر الكفرة وإعلاء كلمة الحق ولو فرضنا في الجهاد. ١٢ أي الجناية وشره الكفرة. ۱۲ المذكور من محدده بواسطة الزجر :أي: منع المتمرّد عن الجناية كالزنا وشرب الخمر، والقصاص مثل الحــدّ وإنما حسن بواسطة زجر الظلمة عن القتل، فافهم. ١٢ (۳) قوله بواسطة دفع شرّ الكفرة لا باعتبار نفسه، فإنّ الجهاد فيه تخريب البلاد وتعذيب الناس وليس оя ذلك حسناً بنفسه، قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «الآدَمِيُّ بُنيَانُ الربِّ ، مَلعُونٌ مِن هَدَمَ بُنْيـــانَ الـــربِّ» وإنما حسن بواسطة كفر الكافر، فإنّ الكفرة أعداء الله تعالى والمسلمين، فلذلك حسن لدفع شـــــرهـم وإعلاء كلمة الحق. ١٢ (٤) قوله: [إلى الحراب] إنما قال: «إلى الحراب» ولم يقل: إلى : شرّ الكفرة تنبيهاً على أن المراد بشر الكفــــرة الحراب، وإنما قال: «لو فرضنا»؛ لأنه خلاف الخبر وهو قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «الْجِهَادُ مَاضٍ إِلَى الْقِيَامَةِ» وإنما قال: «والقريب من هذا النوع» مع أنّ الحسن في هذه الثلث أيضاً بواسطة للفرق بين هــذه الثلث يَوْمِ وبين السعي والوضوء، فإنّ حسن السعي والوضوء بواسطة الجمعة والصلاة، وهما لا يتأديان بالسعى حسن والوضوء، بل بأفعال مقصودة وأقوال معلومة بخلاف الحدود والقصاص والجهاد، فإنّ هذه الثلث بواسطة الزجر عن الجناية وقتل النفس المعصومة وإعلاء كلمة الله وهذه الوسائط تتأدى بنفس الحــــدّ والقصاص والجهاد؛ لأنّ بنفس الحدّ والقصاص يحصل الزجر وبنفس الجهاد يحصل الإعلاء، أو يقال: إنما قال: «والقريب من هذا النوع»؛ لأنّ القسم الأوّل أي: السعي والوضوء كاملاً في كونه حسناً لغيره؛ لأنّ الغير لا يحصل بفعل المأمور به بخلاف هذا القسم :أي: الحدود والقصاص والجهاد، فإن الغير يحصل بفعـــل المأمور به على ما بين آنفاً، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢
Usul al-Shashi with Ahsan al-Hawashi: i.e., good for other than itself. 12 Deterrents legislated for crime, so they are means to prevent crime. 12 (1) Section: The command to do something indicates the goodness of the commanded thing. This type includes the hudud, qisas, and jihad. Indeed, the hadd (punishment) is good by means of deterrence from crime, which is the original purpose of legislation, such as zina and drinking wine. 12 Disbeliever. 12 The crime, and jihad is good by means of repelling the evil of disbelievers and elevating the word of truth. And if we suppose [the absence of] in jihad. 12 That is, the crime and the evil of the disbelievers. 12 Mentioned from its definition, qisas and jihad. 12 By understanding its legislation the intermediate [cause] would not be legislated at all. 12 If the intermediate is absent, that [act] does not remain commanded. Because if there were no crime, the hadd would not be obligatory, and if there were no, while the situation is that he (peace be upon him) said: 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment.' 12 (4) The disbelief that leads to war, jihad is not obligatory upon him. That is, the Imam. 12 For its own self is obviously invalid, as in some marginalia. 12 (1) His statement: [from this type] because the first division, that is, sa'y and wudu, are complete in being good for other than themselves; because the other [goal] is not obtained by the commanded act, unlike this type, i.e., hudud, qisas, and jihad, because the other is obtained by the commanded act. 12 Good in itself. (2) His statement: [by means of deterrence, etc.] with regard to its essence, because the hadd is a punishment and torture for servants, and that is not good in itself, but good by means of deterrence, i.e., preventing the rebellious from crime like zina and drinking wine. And qisas is like the hadd, but good by means of deterring oppressors from killing, so understand. 12 (3) His statement: by means of repelling the evil of disbelievers, not with regard to itself, because jihad involves destruction of lands and torture of people, and that is not good in itself. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The human is the building of the Lord; cursed is the one who destroys the building of the Lord.' Rather, it is good by means of the disbelief of the disbeliever, because the disbelievers are enemies of Allah and the Muslims, so it is good for repelling their evil and elevating the word of truth. 12 (4) His statement: [to war] He said 'to war' and did not say 'to the evil of the disbelievers' to indicate that the intended meaning is the evil of the disbelievers who are at war. And he said 'if we suppose' because it contradicts the report, which is his statement (peace be upon him): 'Jihad continues until the Day of Judgment.' And he said: 'and what is close to this type' although the goodness in these three is also by means, to distinguish between these three and sa'y and wudu. Indeed, the goodness of sa'y and wudu is by means of Friday prayer and prayer, and these two are not fulfilled by sa'y and wudu, but by intended actions and known words. Unlike the hudud, qisas, and jihad, because these three are by means of deterrence from crime, killing of inviolable life, and elevation of the word of Allah, and these means are actualized by the hadd, qisas, and jihad themselves because by the hadd and qisas themselves deterrence occurs, and by jihad itself elevation occurs. Or it is said: He only said 'and what is close to this type' because the first division, i.e., sa'y and wudu, are complete in being good for other than themselves because the other is not obtained by the commanded act, unlike this division, i.e., hudud, qisas, and jihad, because the other is obtained by the commanded act as explained above. As in al-Ma'dan. 12
Source pages p. 114

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi, with its commentary Ahsan al-Hawashi, discusses a fundamental usul principle: when a command (amr) is given for an action, it indicates that the commanded action (al-ma'mur bihi) is ḥasan (good/praiseworthy). However, the text clarifies that this goodness can be either intrinsic (ḥasan li-‘aynihi) or extrinsic (ḥasan li-ghayrihi). The author gives three examples—ḥudūd (fixed punishments), qiṣāṣ (retaliation), and jihād—which are good not in themselves but for their deterrent effects. The commentary explains that ḥudūd involve punishment and torture but become good because they deter crime; similarly, qiṣāṣ deters murder; jihād involves destruction and suffering but is good because it repels the evil of disbelievers and elevates Allah's word. A ḥadīth is cited: 'The human is the building of the Lord; cursed is he who destroys the building of the Lord,' showing jihād is not intrinsically good. The text distinguishes these from acts like sa'y (running between Safa and Marwah) and wuḍū' (ablution), which are also ḥasan li-ghayrihi but differ because the goal (e.g., Friday prayer) is not attained by the act itself, whereas for ḥudūd, the deterrent effect is achieved by the act itself. The commentary also addresses a potential objection: if we suppose the absence of the intermediate cause (e.g., no crime), then the commanded act (ḥadd) would not be obligatory, but jihād is continuous until Judgment Day. This clarifies that the goodness of the act depends on the presence of its purpose. The teacher should emphasize that this principle has practical implications: it distinguishes acts that are inherently commanded from those commanded as means to an end, and it shows how uṣūl scholars categorize actions.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): A command from the Lawgiver; not explicitly defined in this passage, but used as a request for an action.
المأمور به (al-ma'mur bihi): The act that is commanded; its goodness is indicated by the command.
الحسن (al-ḥasan): The attribute of being good or praiseworthy; can be intrinsic (li-'aynihi) or extrinsic (li-ghayrihi).
الحدود (al-ḥudūd): Fixed corporal punishments for major sins like zina and drinking wine; good as deterrents.
الواسطة (al-wāsiṭa): The intermediate cause or purpose that makes an act good extrinsically (e.g., deterrence for ḥudūd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is jihād considered good (ḥasan) despite involving destruction and death?
A) Because it is good in itself.
B) Because it repels the evil of disbelievers and elevates the word of truth.
C) Because it is commanded.
D) Because it brings reward.

Key Takeaway
A command from Allah always indicates that the commanded act is good, but the goodness may be extrinsic, realized through the act's consequences.

Types of Wajib: Ada' and Qada' — Definitions and Subdivisions
Defining ada' and qada' and subdividing ada' into kamil and qasir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of ada' and qada', and distinguish between ada' kamil and ada' qasir using examples from worship.

Core Idea
Ada' delivers the exact wajib; qada' delivers its like; both fulfill the command.

In Hanafi usul, the wajib (obligatory act) commanded by the Lawgiver is classified into two types based on the timing of performance: ada' (timely performance) and qada' (make-up after the time). This passage from Usul al-Shashi provides precise definitions and further divides ada' into complete and deficient forms, helping us understand the degrees of fulfilling an obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wajib
Read the first line: 'الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان أداء وقضاء'. Recognize that the author divides the wajib that is established by a command into two categories: ada' and qada'.
This classification is based on whether the act is performed in its proper time or after it.
2
Analyze the definition of ada'
Find: 'الأداء عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه'. Break it down: 'تسليم' (delivery), 'عين الواجب' (the very wajib), 'إلى مستحقه' (to its rightful recipient). Understand that 'delivery' in acts means performing them, as worship is a right of Allah.
The phrase 'إلى مستحقه' is crucial—without it, a payment to the wrong person would not count as ada'.
3
Analyze the definition of qada'
Find: 'القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه'. Note the key difference: 'مثل الواجب' (a like of the wajib), not 'عين الواجب'. This is because the original exact act is no longer possible after its time has passed.
The commentary clarifies that 'like' means a similar act, not the exact same one.
4
Subdivide ada' into kamil and qasir
Read: 'ثم الأداء نوعان كامل وقاصر'. Understand that complete ada' fulfills all rights and conditions of the commanded act, while deficient ada' lacks some elements. The commentary gives examples like praying at a disliked time or with a sinful imam.
Absolute complete ada' has no deficiency; relative complete ada' has some but is still considered ada'.
5
Apply the definitions to the example of prayer
The passage mentions prayer in congregation as an example. See how the commentary specifies that 'prayer' here means obligatory prayer, and congregation in supererogatory prayers is like an extra finger—not a perfection.
This shows how the definitions are applied to specific acts to determine completeness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان أداء وقضاء، فالأداء عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه والقضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه ثم الأداء نوعان كامل وقاصر فالكامل  مثل: أداء الصلاة في وكذا الصوم. ١٢ (۱) قوله: [نوعان... إلح يعني أنّ الأمر قد يرد لطلب إيقاع فعل وجب في ذمته بوجود سببه ابتداء مــــــن غير سبق فواته كالأمر بإقامة الصلاة، وقد يرد لإيقاع ما سبق فوته كقوله عليه السلام: «فَلْيُصَلِّهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا» قسمى الإيقاع الأوّل أداء والثاني قضاء. ١٢ (۲) قوله: عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب ... إلخ تسليم عين الواجب أو المثل في الأفعــال [ والأعراض إيجادها والإتيان بها، فإنّ العبادة حق الله تعالى فالعبد يؤدّيها ويسلّمها إليه، ولم يعتبر التقييد بالوقت ليعمّ أداء الزكاة والأمانات والمنذورات والكفارات والمراد بالواجب هاهنا ما يعم الفرض أيضاً. ١٢ (۳) قوله: [إلى مستحقه] إنّما زاد هذا اللفظ مع أنه متروك في عبارة كثير من المشائخ؛ لأنه مـــــن تمام حقيقة المحدود؛ إذ التسليم لا بد فيه من تمامه، وتمامه بوجود المسلّم إليه كيف، وإنمــا المأمور به إذا سلّم دراهم دين إلى غير ربّ الدين لا يكون ذلك التسليم أداءً، كذا في بعض الحواشي. ١٢ (٤) قوله: [والقضاء... إلخ ] أي: القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب لا عينه أي: تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أوّلاً في غير ذلك الوقت، وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: «من عنده» ليخرج أداء الظهر أي: ظهر اليوم عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده، بل كلاهما الله تعالى، وإنما لم يقيده لشهرة أمره وكونه مدلولاً عليه بالالتزام كذا في "نور الأنوار". ١٢ (٥) قوله: [فالكامل... إلخ] هو أداء المأمور به على وجه أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه، ولو استوفى بعض حقوقه دون بعض فهو كامل من ذلك الوجه قاصر من هذا الوجه كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة إذا أديت في وقت مكروه أو بإمامة الفاسق أو بترك واجب أو سنة من داخلها أو خارجها، فالكامل المطلق ما لا يترك فيه حق من حقوق الأداء وغيره عن النقصانات كلّها، والكامل الإضافي ما استوفى فيـــه بعضها دون بعض وهو يجامع القاصر. ١٢ (٦) قوله : [أداء الصلاة والمراد بها الصلاة المكتوبة؛ لأنّ الجماعة فيما عداها صفة قصور بمنزلة الإصبع الزائدة، فلو أريد بها مطلق الصلاة فلم يطابق المثال بالممثل، كما لا يخفى. ١٢
Section: The wajib by virtue of a command is of two types: ada' and qada'. Ada' is the delivery of the very wajib to its rightfully entitled person, and qada' is the delivery of the like (mithl) of the wajib to its rightfully entitled person. Then ada' is of two types: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). The complete example is: performing prayer in its time. Likewise fasting. 12 (1) His statement: [two types, etc.] means that the command may come to demand the occurrence of an act that became incumbent in one's liability due to its cause initially without prior expiration, like the command to establish prayer, and it may come to demand the occurrence of what has previously expired, like his statement (peace be upon him): 'Let him pray it when he remembers it.' He called the first occurrence ada' and the second qada'. 12 (2) His statement: 'delivery of the very wajib, etc.' Delivery of the very wajib or its mithl in actions and accidents means bringing them into existence and performing them. Because worship is a right of Allah, so the servant performs it and delivers it to Him. The restriction by time was not considered in order to include the performance of zakat, trusts, vows, and expiations. And the intended meaning of 'wajib' here includes fard as well. 12 (3) His statement: [to its rightfully entitled person] He added this phrase even though it is omitted in the expression of many scholars because it is part of the complete reality of the thing defined; since delivery necessarily requires completion, and its completion is by the presence of the one to whom it is delivered. Otherwise, if the commanded person delivers dirhams that are owed to someone other than the creditor, that delivery is not ada'. As in some marginalia. 12 (4) His statement: [And qada', etc.] That is, qada' is delivery of the like (mithl) of the wajib, not the very wajib. That is, the delivery of that wajib which was originally obligated in a time other than its time. And it would have been appropriate to restrict it with his statement: 'from himself' to exclude the performance of zuhr today for yesterday's zuhr; because it is not from himself, rather both are for Allah. But he did not restrict it due to its fame and being indicated by implication. As in Nur al-Anwar. 12 (5) His statement: [So the complete, etc.] It is performing the commanded act in a manner legislated with fulfilling all its rights. If some of its rights are fulfilled and some are not, it is complete in that aspect and deficient in this aspect, like performing prayer in congregation when performed at a disliked time, or with an imam who is a sinner, or leaving a wajib or sunnah from within or outside. So the absolute complete is what leaves no right among the rights of performance and others from all deficiencies, and the relative complete is what fulfills some of them while omitting others, and it coexists with the deficient. 12 (6) His statement: [performing prayer] and by it is meant the obligatory prayer; because congregation in other than it is a quality of deficiency like an extra finger. So if absolute prayer were intended, the example would not correspond to the example, as is clear. 12
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi with commentary defines the types of wajib (obligatory act) by virtue of a command. It explains that wajib is divided into two categories: ada' (performance) and qada' (make-up). Ada' is defined as delivering the very same wajib (عين الواجب) to its rightful recipient (مستحق), while qada' is delivering a like (مثل) of the wajib. For example, performing the zuhr prayer in its time is ada', but if one misses it and prays later, that is qada'. The commentary clarifies that 'delivery' in acts means bringing them into existence. It also notes that the phrase 'to its rightful recipient' is important because without it, a payment to the wrong person would not count as ada'. The definition of qada' involves delivering a 'like' because the original exact act is no longer possible. Then ada' is further subdivided into kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient). Complete ada' fulfills all rights and conditions of the act, such as performing prayer with all its obligations and sunnats on time. Deficient ada' lacks some elements, e.g., praying in a disliked time or with an sinful imam. The commentary distinguishes absolute complete (which has no deficiency) from relative complete (which has some deficiencies but is still considered complete in some respects). The example given is prayer in congregation; the commentary specifies that the intended prayer is the obligatory prayer because congregation in other prayers is like an extra finger—i.e., not a perfection. This passage is foundational for understanding how Hanafi usul classifies acts and the nuances of fulfilling obligations.

Key Terms
الأداء (al-adā'): تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه - delivery of the very wajib to its rightful recipient, i.e., performing the act exactly as required.
القضاء (al-qaḍā'): تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه - delivery of the like (mithl) of the wajib, i.e., performing a similar act to make up for a missed obligation.
الأداء الكامل (al-adā' al-kāmil): Complete performance that fulfills all rights and conditions of the commanded act, without any deficiency.
الأداء القاصر (al-adā' al-qāṣir): Deficient performance that lacks some rights or conditions, but is still considered ada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does qada' (make-up) involve delivering?
A) The exact same wajib (عين الواجب) to its recipient.
B) A like (مثل) of the wajib to its recipient.
C) Any similar act without conditions.
D) Nothing; qada' is only for prayers.

Key Takeaway
Ada' and qada' are the two types of wajib by command: ada' delivers the very wajib in its time, qada' delivers a like after the time; ada' can be complete or deficient depending on fulfillment of rights.

Definitions of Ada and Qada
Defining ada and qada as two types of wajib with subcategories and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define ada and qada according to Hanafi usul, and distinguish between them based on the key element of delivering the exact wajib versus its equivalent, and identify the condition of delivery to the rightful recipient.

Core Idea
Ada delivers the exact wajib; qada delivers its equivalent — the rightful recipient completes the definition.

The Hanafi school classifies all wajib acts by command into two fundamental categories: ada and qada. This distinction is not merely about timing but about the very object of delivery. By understanding these definitions, you will be able to analyze how each obligation is fulfilled and when a person is discharged.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of wajib
The text begins by stating that the wajib by command is of two types: ada and qada. This sets up the entire discussion.
Note that 'wajib' here includes fard, as the hashiya clarifies.
2
Extract the definition of ada
Ada is defined as 'تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه' (delivery of the exact wajib to its rightful recipient). Focus on the word 'عين' (exact).
3
Extract the definition of qada
Qada is defined as 'تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه' (delivery of the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient). Focus on the word 'مثل' (equivalent).
4
Understand the necessity of 'to its rightful recipient'
The hashiya explains that this phrase is essential because delivery to the wrong person does not constitute ada. Without it, the definition would be incomplete.
This condition ensures the obligation is actually fulfilled.
5
Relate to the broader application
The hashiya notes that these definitions apply to all wajib acts, including prayers, zakat, trusts, etc. The concept of 'delivery' in acts means performing them.
The definition is not limited to physical objects.

Source Text

فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان أداء وقضاء، فالأداء عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه والقضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه ثم الأداء نوعان كامل وقاصر فالكامل مثل: أداء الصلاة في وقتها بالجماعة أو الطواف متوضئا وتسليم المبيع سليما كما اقتضاه العقد إلى المشتري وتسليم الغاصب العين المغصوبة كما غصبها وحكم هذا النوع أن يحكم بالخروج عن العهدة به، وعلى هذا قلنا الغاصب إذا باع المغصوب من مالكه أو وهب له وسلمه إليه يخرج عن العهدة ويكون ذلك أداءً لحقه ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة، ولو غصب طعاما فأطعمه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه طعامه، أو غصب ثوبا فألبسه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه ثوبه يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه، والمشتري في البيع الفاسد لو أعار المبيع من البائع أو رهنه عنده أو اجره منه او باعة المبيع البائع وهبه له وسلمه يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة ونحوه. وأما الأداء القاصر فهو...

ثم قال في الحاشية: (1) قوله: [نوعان... إلخ يعني أنّ الأمر قد يرد لطلب إيقاع فعل وجب في ذمته بوجود سببه ابتداء من غير سبق فواته كالأمر بإقامة الصلاة، وقد يرد لإيقاع ما سبق فوته كقوله عليه السلام: «فَلْيُصَلِّهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا» قسمى الإيقاع الأوّل أداء والثاني قضاء. (2) قوله: عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب ... إلخ تسليم عين الواجب أو المثل في الأفعـال والأعراض إيجادها والإتيان بها، فإنّ العبادة حق الله تعالى فالعبد يؤدّيها ويسلّمها إليه، ولم يعتبر التقييد بالوقت ليعمّ أداء الزكاة والأمانات والمنذورات والكفارات والمراد بالواجب هاهنا ما يعم الفرض أيضاً. (3) قوله: [إلى مستحقه] إنّما زاد هذا اللفظ مع أنه متروك في عبارة كثير من المشائخ؛ لأنه من تمام حقيقة المحدود؛ إذ التسليم لا بد فيه من تمامه، وتمامه بوجود المسلّم إليه كيف، وإنما المأمور به إذا سلّم دراهم دين إلى غير ربّ الدين لا يكون ذلك التسليم أداءً. (4) قوله: [والقضاء... إلخ ] أي: القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب لا عينه أي: تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أوّلاً في غير ذلك الوقت، وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: «من عنده» ليخرج أداء الظهر أي: ظهر اليوم عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده، بل كلاهما الله تعالى، وإنما لم يقيده لشهرة أمره وكونه مدلولاً عليه بالالتزام. (5) قوله: [فالكامل... إلخ] هو أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه، ولو استوفى بعض حقوقه دون بعض فهو كامل من ذلك الوجه قاصر من هذا الوجه كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة إذا أديت في وقت مكروه أو بإمامة الفاسق أو بترك واجب أو سنة من داخلها أو خارجها، فالكامل المطلق ما لا يترك فيه حق من حقوق الأداء وغيره عن النقصانات كلّها، والكامل الإضافي ما استوفى فيه بعضها دون بعض وهو يجامع القاصر. (6) قوله : [أداء الصلاة والمراد بها الصلاة المكتوبة؛ لأنّ الجماعة فيما عداها صفة قصور بمنزلة الإصبع الزائدة، فلو أريد بها مطلق الصلاة فلم يطابق المثال بالممثل.

(1) قوله: [أو الطواف... إلخ لقوله عليه السلام: «الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْت صَلَاةٌ» والصلاة بدون الطهارة لا تجوز، لكنه يجزئ بدون الطهارة أيضاً لإطلاق النص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ العتيق ﴾ [الحج : ٢٩]. (2) قوله: [أداءً لحقه هذا إذا لم يحدث فيه ما يقطع حق المالك، فأما إذا حدث فيه ما يقطع حقه بأن كان دقيقاً فخبزه فأطعمه، أو لحماً فشوّاه ثم أطعمه لا يبرأ عن الضمان بالاتفاق؛ لأنه ملك بهذه التصرفات. (3) قوله: [في البيع الفاسد] اعلم أن البيع الفاسد كالبيع بالخمر والخنزير والبيع بشرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لأحد العاقدين أو المعقود عليه وهو من أهل الاستحقاق كما إذا باع عبداً بشرط أن يعتقه المشتري أو يدبّره أو يكاتبه أو أمة على أن يستولدها المشتري، فإذا قبض المبيع المشتري في البيع الفاسد يكون المبيع مضموناً في يده، ولكلّ واحد من المتعاقدين فسخه دفعاً للفساد ويجب على المشتري ردّ المبيع إلى البائع، فإذا أعار المشتري المبيع من البائع أو رهنه المشتري عند البائع أو أعطى المشتري المبيع للبائع بالأجرة أو وهب المشتري المبيع للبائع وقبض البائع يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه؛ لأنه تسليم عين الواجب.
Chapter: The wajib by command is of two types: ada and qada. Ada is the delivery of the exact wajib to its rightful recipient, and qada is the delivery of the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient. Then ada is of two types: complete and deficient. The complete is like: performing prayer in its time with congregation, or performing tawaf with ablution, and delivering the sold item soundly as required by the contract to the buyer, and the usurper delivering the usurped item as it was usurped. The ruling of this type is that one is judged to have been discharged of responsibility by it. Based on this we say: if the usurper sells the usurped item to its owner, or gives it as a gift to him and delivers it to him, he is discharged of responsibility and that is considered ada of his right, and what he explicitly stated of sale or gift is nullified. And if he usurped food and fed it to its owner while the owner did not know it was his food, or usurped a garment and clothed its owner with it while the owner did not know it was his garment, that is considered ada of his right. And the buyer in an invalid sale, if he lends the sold item to the seller, or pawns it with him, or rents it from him, or sells the sold item back to the seller, or gives it as a gift to him and delivers it, that is considered ada of his right, and what he explicitly stated of sale, gift, etc. is nullified. As for deficient ada, it is...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the two categories of wajib (obligatory acts) in terms of their fulfillment: ada (performance within the prescribed time) and qada (make-up after the time has passed). The author first defines ada as delivering the exact wajib to its rightful recipient, and qada as delivering its equivalent. Then he divides ada into two types: kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient). Complete ada involves fulfilling the wajib in the prescribed manner with all its conditions and rights, such as praying the obligatory prayer in its time with congregation, performing tawaf with wudu, delivering sold goods soundly, and a usurper returning the exact usurped item. The legal effect of complete ada is that the person is considered discharged of the obligation. The author then applies this principle to cases of usurpation (ghasp) and invalid sale (bay' fasid): if a usurper returns the usurped item to its owner through a sale or gift, the transaction is void but the return itself constitutes valid ada. Similarly, in a voidable sale, if the buyer returns the item to the seller through various transactions (loan, pawn, rent, sale, gift), the return is valid ada despite the underlying contract being void. The deficient ada (not fully described in this passage) would be when some rights are missing, e.g., prayer without congregation or with an imperfect condition. The hashiya further explains that the term 'wajib' here includes fard, and that delivering to the rightful recipient is essential; delivering to the wrong person does not count as ada.

Key Terms
أداء (ada): تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه (delivery of the exact wajib to its rightful recipient)
قضاء (qada): تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه (delivery of the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient)
كامل (kamil): أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه (performing the commanded act as legislated with all its rights)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in this passage, what is 'qada'?
A) Delivering the exact wajib to its rightful recipient
B) Delivering the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient
C) Performing an act in its time
D) Performing an act after its time

Key Takeaway
Ada delivers the exact obligation; qada delivers its equivalent both must reach the rightful recipient to discharge the duty.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate
8 min
Complete Ada and Its Legal Effect of Discharge
Defining ada and qada as two types of wajib with subcategories and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify examples of complete ada and state the legal effect that the obligation is discharged, even when the means of return (e.g., void sale) are invalid.

Core Idea
Complete ada discharges the obligation; void transactions do not prevent discharge.

The text provides several concrete examples of complete ada, all of which result in discharge from responsibility. A key insight is that if the exact wajib is delivered to the rightful recipient, the obligation is fulfilled regardless of whether the mechanism of delivery (e.g., a sale or gift) is valid or void. This lesson explores those examples and the underlying reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Review the definition of complete ada
Complete ada is performing the commanded act as legislated with all its rights. This includes fulfilling conditions and obligations.
The hashiya later divides complete ada into absolute and relative; here we focus on the examples given.
2
List the examples of complete ada
The text gives four main examples: (1) prayer in time with congregation, (2) tawaf with wudu, (3) delivering sold item soundly, (4) usurper returning the exact usurped item.
Note that tawaf without wudu is not complete ada, but the text later notes it is valid due to a Quranic text.
3
Identify the legal effect
The ruling for complete ada is 'al-hukmu bi al-khuruj an al-uhdah bihi' — one is judged to have been discharged of responsibility.
This applies even if the underlying transaction is void.
4
Examine the usurper cases
If a usurper sells or gives the usurped item to the owner, the return is considered ada. The sale/gift is void but the delivery itself suffices.
This applies even if the owner does not know the item is his, as long as he physically receives it.
5
Examine the invalid sale case
Similarly, a buyer in an invalid sale (bay' fasid) who returns the item to the seller via any transaction (lend, pawn, rent, sale, gift) has performed ada of his right to return.
The condition is that the owner's right is not cut by prior consumption.

Source Text

Commentary

البيع الفاسد (al-bay' al-fasid): A sale that is invalid due to a condition that benefits one party, but the essential elements of sale are present; it is voidable and requires return of the item.

Hashiya Refinements: Complete, Deficient, and Subtypes of Ada
Defining ada and qada as two types of wajib with subcategories and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between absolute complete ada and relative complete ada, and identify deficient ada according to the hashiya's analysis.

Core Idea
Complete ada can be absolute (all rights) or relative (some rights); deficient ada coexists with relative.

The hashiya (commentary) enriches the classification of ada by introducing two subtypes of complete ada: absolute (kamil mutlaq) and relative (kamil idafi). It also clarifies that deficient ada (qasir) does not necessarily invalidate the act but indicates imperfection. This lesson unpacks these distinctions and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Recall the base division of ada into kamil and qasir
The matn states that ada is of two types: complete (kamil) and deficient (qasir). The hashiya expands on this.
Complete ada is defined as performing the act with all its rights.
2
Read the hashiya's definition of kamil
The hashiya says: 'هو أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه' — performing the commanded act in the legislated manner with all its rights.
3
Identify the two subtypes of kamil
The hashiya divides kamil into 'kamil mutlaq' (absolute) and 'kamil idafi' (relative). Mutlaq has no rights missing; idafi has some rights fulfilled and some not.
The hashiya gives an example: prayer with congregation in a disliked time or with a sinful imam is kamil from one aspect (congregation) and qasir from another (time or imamate).
4
Understand the relationship between kamil idafi and qasir
The hashiya states that kamil idafi 'yujami' al-qasir' — it coexists with deficient. That is, an act can be both complete in some respects and deficient in others.
This is not a contradiction; it means the act is evaluated from multiple perspectives.
5
Apply to the examples
For instance, praying with congregation but at a disliked time: it is complete (because congregation is a right) but deficient (because of the disliked time). This is relative completeness.
The hashiya notes that congregation is a right only for obligatory prayers, not for nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل الواجب بحكم الأمر نوعان أداء وقضاء، فالأداء عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه والقضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه ثم الأداء نوعان كامل وقاصر فالكامل مثل: أداء الصلاة في وقتها بالجماعة أو الطواف متوضئا وتسليم المبيع سليما كما اقتضاه العقد إلى المشتري وتسليم الغاصب العين المغصوبة كما غصبها وحكم هذا النوع أن يحكم بالخروج عن العهدة به، وعلى هذا قلنا الغاصب إذا باع المغصوب من مالكه أو وهب له وسلمه إليه يخرج عن العهدة ويكون ذلك أداءً لحقه ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة، ولو غصب طعاما فأطعمه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه طعامه، أو غصب ثوبا فألبسه مالكه وهو لا يدري أنه ثوبه يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه، والمشتري في البيع الفاسد لو أعار المبيع من البائع أو رهنه عنده أو اجره منه او باعة المبيع البائع وهبه له وسلمه يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه ويلغو ما صرح به من البيع والهبة ونحوه. وأما الأداء القاصر فهو...

ثم قال في الحاشية: (1) قوله: [نوعان... إلخ يعني أنّ الأمر قد يرد لطلب إيقاع فعل وجب في ذمته بوجود سببه ابتداء من غير سبق فواته كالأمر بإقامة الصلاة، وقد يرد لإيقاع ما سبق فوته كقوله عليه السلام: «فَلْيُصَلِّهَا إِذَا ذَكَرَهَا» قسمى الإيقاع الأوّل أداء والثاني قضاء. (2) قوله: عبارة عن تسليم عين الواجب ... إلخ تسليم عين الواجب أو المثل في الأفعـال والأعراض إيجادها والإتيان بها، فإنّ العبادة حق الله تعالى فالعبد يؤدّيها ويسلّمها إليه، ولم يعتبر التقييد بالوقت ليعمّ أداء الزكاة والأمانات والمنذورات والكفارات والمراد بالواجب هاهنا ما يعم الفرض أيضاً. (3) قوله: [إلى مستحقه] إنّما زاد هذا اللفظ مع أنه متروك في عبارة كثير من المشائخ؛ لأنه من تمام حقيقة المحدود؛ إذ التسليم لا بد فيه من تمامه، وتمامه بوجود المسلّم إليه كيف، وإنما المأمور به إذا سلّم دراهم دين إلى غير ربّ الدين لا يكون ذلك التسليم أداءً. (4) قوله: [والقضاء... إلخ ] أي: القضاء عبارة عن تسليم مثل الواجب لا عينه أي: تسليم ذلك الواجب الذي وجب أوّلاً في غير ذلك الوقت، وكان ينبغي أن يقيده بقوله: «من عنده» ليخرج أداء الظهر أي: ظهر اليوم عن ظهر أمسه؛ لأنه ليس من عنده، بل كلاهما الله تعالى، وإنما لم يقيده لشهرة أمره وكونه مدلولاً عليه بالالتزام. (5) قوله: [فالكامل... إلخ] هو أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه، ولو استوفى بعض حقوقه دون بعض فهو كامل من ذلك الوجه قاصر من هذا الوجه كأداء الصلاة بالجماعة إذا أديت في وقت مكروه أو بإمامة الفاسق أو بترك واجب أو سنة من داخلها أو خارجها، فالكامل المطلق ما لا يترك فيه حق من حقوق الأداء وغيره عن النقصانات كلّها، والكامل الإضافي ما استوفى فيه بعضها دون بعض وهو يجامع القاصر. (6) قوله : [أداء الصلاة والمراد بها الصلاة المكتوبة؛ لأنّ الجماعة فيما عداها صفة قصور بمنزلة الإصبع الزائدة، فلو أريد بها مطلق الصلاة فلم يطابق المثال بالممثل.

(1) قوله: [أو الطواف... إلخ لقوله عليه السلام: «الطَّوَافُ بِالْبَيْت صَلَاةٌ» والصلاة بدون الطهارة لا تجوز، لكنه يجزئ بدون الطهارة أيضاً لإطلاق النص وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ وَلْيَطَّوَّفُوا بِالْبَيْتِ العتيق ﴾ [الحج : ٢٩]. (2) قوله: [أداءً لحقه هذا إذا لم يحدث فيه ما يقطع حق المالك، فأما إذا حدث فيه ما يقطع حقه بأن كان دقيقاً فخبزه فأطعمه، أو لحماً فشوّاه ثم أطعمه لا يبرأ عن الضمان بالاتفاق؛ لأنه ملك بهذه التصرفات. (3) قوله: [في البيع الفاسد] اعلم أن البيع الفاسد كالبيع بالخمر والخنزير والبيع بشرط لا يقتضيه العقد وفيه منفعة لأحد العاقدين أو المعقود عليه وهو من أهل الاستحقاق كما إذا باع عبداً بشرط أن يعتقه المشتري أو يدبّره أو يكاتبه أو أمة على أن يستولدها المشتري، فإذا قبض المبيع المشتري في البيع الفاسد يكون المبيع مضموناً في يده، ولكلّ واحد من المتعاقدين فسخه دفعاً للفساد ويجب على المشتري ردّ المبيع إلى البائع، فإذا أعار المشتري المبيع من البائع أو رهنه المشتري عند البائع أو أعطى المشتري المبيع للبائع بالأجرة أو وهب المشتري المبيع للبائع وقبض البائع يكون ذلك أداءً لحقه؛ لأنه تسليم عين الواجب.
Chapter: The wajib by command is of two types: ada and qada. Ada is the delivery of the exact wajib to its rightful recipient, and qada is the delivery of the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient. Then ada is of two types: complete and deficient. The complete is like: performing prayer in its time with congregation, or performing tawaf with ablution, and delivering the sold item soundly as required by the contract to the buyer, and the usurper delivering the usurped item as it was usurped. The ruling of this type is that one is judged to have been discharged of responsibility by it. Based on this we say: if the usurper sells the usurped item to its owner, or gives it as a gift to him and delivers it to him, he is discharged of responsibility and that is considered ada of his right, and what he explicitly stated of sale or gift is nullified. And if he usurped food and fed it to its owner while the owner did not know it was his food, or usurped a garment and clothed its owner with it while the owner did not know it was his garment, that is considered ada of his right. And the buyer in an invalid sale, if he lends the sold item to the seller, or pawns it with him, or rents it from him, or sells the sold item back to the seller, or gives it as a gift to him and delivers it, that is considered ada of his right, and what he explicitly stated of sale, gift, etc. is nullified. As for deficient ada, it is...
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the two categories of wajib (obligatory acts) in terms of their fulfillment: ada (performance within the prescribed time) and qada (make-up after the time has passed). The author first defines ada as delivering the exact wajib to its rightful recipient, and qada as delivering its equivalent. Then he divides ada into two types: kamil (complete) and qasir (deficient). Complete ada involves fulfilling the wajib in the prescribed manner with all its conditions and rights, such as praying the obligatory prayer in its time with congregation, performing tawaf with wudu, delivering sold goods soundly, and a usurper returning the exact usurped item. The legal effect of complete ada is that the person is considered discharged of the obligation. The author then applies this principle to cases of usurpation (ghasp) and invalid sale (bay' fasid): if a usurper returns the usurped item to its owner through a sale or gift, the transaction is void but the return itself constitutes valid ada. Similarly, in a voidable sale, if the buyer returns the item to the seller through various transactions (loan, pawn, rent, sale, gift), the return is valid ada despite the underlying contract being void. The deficient ada (not fully described in this passage) would be when some rights are missing, e.g., prayer without congregation or with an imperfect condition. The hashiya further explains that the term 'wajib' here includes fard, and that delivering to the rightful recipient is essential; delivering to the wrong person does not count as ada.

Key Terms
أداء (ada): تسليم عين الواجب إلى مستحقه (delivery of the exact wajib to its rightful recipient)
قضاء (qada): تسليم مثل الواجب إلى مستحقه (delivery of the equivalent of the wajib to its rightful recipient)
كامل (kamil): أداء المأمور به على وجه شرع عليه مع إيفاء جميع حقوقه (performing the commanded act as legislated with all its rights)
الكامل المطلق (al-kamil al-mutlaq): Absolute complete: no right is left unfulfilled.
الكامل الإضافي (al-kamil al-idafi): Relative complete: some rights fulfilled, some not.
القاصر (al-qasir): Deficient ada: when rights are lacking to a degree that makes the act imperfect but still valid if the essentials are present.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hashiya, what is the difference between absolute complete ada and relative complete ada?
A) Absolute complete is for prayers; relative complete is for other acts
B) Absolute complete has no rights missing; relative complete has some rights missing
C) Absolute complete is valid; relative complete is invalid
D) They are the same thing

Key Takeaway
Complete ada can be absolute (all rights) or relative (some rights); relative ada coexists with deficiency.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
