(1) His statement: [with a bow... etc.] For hunting with this bow, even if it is forbidden, yet the legal rulings follow from it: permissibility of the game, ownership, and other things. So it is in al-Ma'din. (12)
(2) His statement: [and slaughtering... etc.] For slaughtering with this knife, even if it is forbidden, yet the permissibility of the slaughtered animal follows from it, etc. (12)
(3) His statement: [and prayer... etc.] For prayer in usurped land, even if it is forbidden, yet the permissibility of prayer follows from it; however it is disliked due to the associated evil. If it is said: What is the difference between intercourse with a menstruating woman and prayer in usurped land, the former being forbidden and the latter disliked, while the reason for its evil is harm and occupation of another's right associated with it? It is said: Analogy would require dislike for intercourse with a menstruating woman, but it is forbidden by consensus or text contrary to analogy. So it is in the books of usul. (12)
(4) His statement: [and selling... etc.] For selling at this time, even if it is prohibited, yet it conveys ownership and other rulings of sale. Moreover, the prohibition in the mentioned matters is because they involve occupying another's property and using it without permission. So understand and do not slip. So it is said. (12)
(5) His statement: [By consideration] That is, the prohibition of the act does not negate the establishment of rulings, or that prohibition of legal acts requires the preservation of legality. So it is in al-Ma'din. (12)
(6) His statement: [the sinful person is among the people of testimony] An objection was raised that deriving this issue from the principle that prohibition requires preservation of legality is problematic, for the prohibited thing is accepting testimony. This principle would require that accepting their testimony is lawful in its essence but not in its attribute. Thus their acceptance should be valid for establishing the right of another, either it is invalid entirely and not testimony in its essence, and that is not a consequence of this principle. The answer: That acceptance or non-acceptance of testimony entails the eligibility for testimony, so the prohibition of accepting testimony is a prohibition regarding their eligibility, and it requires establishing their eligibility for testimony. So this issue is among the consequences of this principle by this path. So it is in al-Multaqat. (12)
(7) His statement: [among the people of testimony...] One may say: Testimony is information based on knowledge, and that is conceivable from a sinful person, but that does not necessitate eligibility for testimony such that the sinful person is among its people. Otherwise, it would follow that a child and a slave are among its people, because they too are able to give information based on their knowledge. The answer: That is accepted, but the eligibility for testimony in a witness is a condition by consensus. Because testimony is the enforcement of a statement over others, which is inconceivable except for one who has authority. That is by eligibility, which is not present in a child or a slave, unlike the sinful person, for it is present. And because it is by legal responsibility and freedom, and both are realized in the sinful person. (12)

Meaning their kind, so it includes two. (12) By the testimony of sinful persons, because the prohibition of accepting testimony without testimony is impossible. And indeed their testimony is not accepted due to a defect in performance, not due to lack of testimony at all. And upon this, li'an is not obligatory for them, because that is performing testimony, and there is no performance with sin, because in it there is bearing of it. And it is five testimonies, the fifth of which is the curse or wrath. (12) Among its people, because they too are able to inform based on their knowledge. And it was answered: This is granted, but eligibility for testimony in a witness is a condition by consensus, because testimony is the enforcement of a statement over others, which is inconceivable except for one who has authority. That is by eligibility, which is not in a child or a slave, unlike the sinful person, for it is present. And because it is by legal responsibility and freedom, and both are realized in the sinful person. (12)
(1) His statement: [By testimony of sinful persons even if a man marries a woman in the presence of two sinful witnesses, that marriage is legally established. Even if the two contractors come before the judge and inform of the marriage by their testimony, the judge must establish that marriage, because they are among the people of testimony by virtue of the prohibition, based on the principle that prohibition of legal acts requires the preservation of legality. For the prohibition of accepting testimony without testimony is impossible, because acceptance or non-acceptance of a thing is only conceivable after the existence of that thing. So it is established that they are among the people of testimony. (12)
(2) His statement: [without testimony is impossible, because if their testimony were not testimony at all, the prohibition of accepting it would be inconceivable. Then it is objected: Since sinful persons are among the people of testimony, their testimony should be accepted. He answered with his statement: “And indeed it is not accepted... etc.” So it is in al-Ma'din. (12)
(3) His statement: [li'an] Its explanation: If a man accuses his wife of adultery, and both are among the people of testimony, and the wife is one whose accuser would be punished with hadd, i.e., she is chaste from adultery, and she demands the legal consequence of the accusation, then li'an is required of him. Li'an linguistically means expulsion and distance. In law, it is testimonies emphasized by oaths accompanied by cursing and wrath, serving in place of the hadd punishment for slander in his case and in place of the hadd punishment for adultery in her case. The description of li'an: The judge begins with the husband, who testifies four times, each time saying: “I testify by Allah that I am among the truthful in what I accused her of, adultery,” pointing to her in all of that. And he says the fifth time: “May the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars.” Then the woman testifies four times, each time saying: “I testify by Allah that he is among the liars in what he accused me of, adultery.” And she says the fifth time: “May the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful in what he accused me of, adultery.” So it is said. (12)
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This is a foundational usul rule: prohibition (nahy) related to external circumstances does not nullify the fundamental validity (mashru'iyya) of an act. The text provides four examples: hunting with a usurped bow, slaughtering with a usurped knife, praying on usurped land, and selling during the Friday call to prayer. In each case, the act is prohibited (haram or makruh) due to the sin of using another’s property without permission or neglecting a religious duty, yet the intended legal effect occurs—the game becomes halal, the meat becomes halal, the prayer fulfills the obligation, and the sale transfers ownership. The key principle is that the prohibition attaches to an external attribute (e.g., usurpation, time), not to the essence of the act itself. This is then applied to the verse on accepting testimony from those punished for slander (Surah al-Nur: 4). The text argues that the fasiq (sinner) remains ‘from the people of testimony’ (ahl al-shahada) because the prohibition is on accepting their testimony, not on their capacity to testify. The capacity remains, but their testimony is not accepted due to a defect in performance (fasad fi al-ada). This is further illustrated by the case of li'an (mutual imprecation), where a husband accusing his wife must perform li'an even if he is fasiq, because the testimony is valid in essence.

Key Terms
النهي (al-nahy): A demand to abstain from an act, indicating prohibition (tahrīm) or dislike (karāha) depending on context.
المشروعية (al-mashru'iyya): The fundamental legality or validity of an act in Islamic law, independent of external prohibitions.
أهل الشهادة (ahl al-shahada): Persons who possess the legal capacity to testify; they meet the conditions of being adult, free, Muslim, and of upright character (adāla) in essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is a marriage witnessed by two sinful men valid?
A) Because the prohibition on accepting their testimony removes their eligibility
B) Because the prohibition implies their eligibility, and the marriage's validity is not dependent on acceptance of testimony
C) Because sinful men are not actually prohibited from testifying
D) Because the marriage contract does not require witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that external prohibition does not nullify fundamental legality is derived from the logical implication of prohibition itself and is applied to uphold the validity of acts like marriage with fasig witnesses.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Prohibition Implies Existence: Testimony of Sinners
Rational proof linking prohibition to existence of testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that a prohibition (nahy) logically implies the existence of the prohibited act, and distinguish between eligibility (ahliyyah) and acceptance (qabul) in the context of testimony.

Core Idea
A prohibition cannot exist without the thing prohibited — sinners have capacity but their testimony is rejected due to corruption in performance.

This passage introduces a fundamental usul principle: prohibition (nahy) necessarily implies that the prohibited act exists. The Hanafi school applies this to the case of accepting testimony from sinners (fussaq). Understanding this logical inference is key to grasping how the Sharia treats sinful witnesses — they are not incapable of testifying, but their sin prevents acceptance. We will work through the rational proof, the distinction between eligibility and performance, and the practical implications for acts like marriage and li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act
The text prohibits accepting testimony from sinners. Determine what act is being prohibited — it is 'accepting testimony' (qabul al-shahada). This presupposes that there is testimony to accept.
The prohibition is on acceptance, not on the act of testifying itself.
2
Apply the rational argument (dalil aqli)
The author argues: 'Prohibition of accepting testimony without testimony is impossible.' That is, you cannot logically prohibit something that does not exist. Therefore, the very prohibition proves that sinners' statements are indeed testimony (shahada) in the legal sense.
This is a qat'i (definitive) rational proof in Hanafi usul.
3
Distinguish eligibility from acceptance
The text explains why testimony is not accepted: 'due to corruption in performance (fasad fi al-ada'), not due to lack of testimony at all.' Sinners have the capacity (ahliyyah) to testify — they are adult, free, Muslim — but their sin corrupts the act of testifying, making their testimony unacceptable.
This distinction is crucial: eligibility is a condition for the existence of testimony; sin is a preventer of its acceptance.
4
Apply the rule to li'an
The passage mentions that sinners are not required to perform li'an (mutual imprecation) because li'an involves performing testimony (shahada), and with sin there is no valid performance. This confirms that their testimony is legally recognized but practically ineffective.
Li'an is a special case: it requires witnesses, but sinners cannot fulfill it due to the same corruption in performance.
5
Derive the practical consequence for marriage
The commentary gives an example: if two sinful witnesses attend a marriage contract, the marriage is valid and the judge must affirm it if the parties inform him. This is because the prohibition of accepting their testimony does not negate the existence of their testimony, so the marriage's basic conditions are met.
The ruling: the marriage is sahih (valid) but the witnesses' sin means they cannot later enforce the testimony in court.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the effect of prohibition (nahy) in Sharia, specifically regarding the testimony of sinners (fussaq). The author establishes that the very existence of a prohibition against accepting testimony implies that the testimony is considered legally valid testimony; otherwise, the prohibition would be meaningless. This is a rational argument (dalil aqli). However, the testimony is not accepted due to corruption in performance (fasad fi al-ada'), not due to lack of eligibility (ahliyyah). This distinction is crucial: sinners have the capacity to testify, but their testimony is rejected because of their sinfulness. The passage then applies this rule to the case of li'an (mutual imprecation) in accusations of adultery: sinners do not perform li'an because that would be performing testimony, and they cannot perform testimony due to their sin. The commentary expands on the logical reasoning, explaining that if sinners were not qualified at all, the prohibition of accepting their testimony would be impossible. It also provides a detailed description of the li'an procedure. The key point is that prohibition does not negate the existence of the thing prohibited; rather, it presupposes it.

Key Terms
النهي (al-nahy): A legal prohibition that necessarily implies the existence of the prohibited act; otherwise the prohibition would be meaningless.
الشهادة (al-shahada): Testimony; a statement of knowledge that legally binds others; requires eligibility (ahliyyah) in the witness.
الفسق (al-fisq): Sinfulness; deviation from obedience; in legal context, a preventer of acceptance of testimony but not of eligibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, why is the testimony of a sinful person (fasiq) not accepted?
A) Because they are not qualified for testimony at all.
B) Because of corruption in their performance (fasad fi al-ada').
C) Because they cannot be trusted in any matter.
D) Because the prohibition of accepting testimony negates the existence of their testimony.

Key Takeaway
A prohibition (nahy) in Sharia logically implies that the prohibited act exists, so sinners have legal capacity to testify but their testimony is rejected due to sin corrupting performance.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Ruling on Menstruating Woman's Prayer Obligation at the End of Time
Deriving ruling on prayer obligation for menstruating woman when bleeding stops within ten days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principles of takhsis and taqyid to derive the ruling for a menstruating woman's prayer obligation and evaluate the use of qiyas based on imagined ability.

Core Idea
Imagined ability suffices for obligation: a menstruating woman must pray if enough time remains for ghusl and takbir.

In this passage from Usul al-Shashi, we examine how the Hanafi school derives the ruling for a menstruating woman whose bleeding stops within ten days at the end of prayer time. The derivation uses takhsis (exception) to exempt her during bleeding, then taqyid (condition) to require prayer only if time remains. The reasoning relies on the concept of imagined ability (qudra mutawaffira), supported by qiyas from the story of Prophet Sulayman. This lesson walks through the derivation and explains the subtle distinction between ability for obligation and ability for performance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule and Its Exception
Recognize that the general rule is that every Muslim who is in a state of purity must pray. The menstruating woman is excepted (takhsis) from this rule during her bleeding.
This exception is a concession (rukhsa).
2
Identify the Condition for Obligation
When the bleeding stops within ten days, the exception ends, but the obligation is conditioned on the existence of ability. The condition here is that enough time remains (from the end of her bleeding to the end of the prayer time) to perform ghusl and say takbirat al-ihram.
This is a taqyid (restriction) on the obligation.
3
Analyze the Reasoning: Imagined Ability
The Hanafi school considers that the obligation of prayer requires only imagined ability (qudra mutawaffira), not actual performance. This is derived from the story of Prophet Sulayman when the sun was held back for him to make up a missed prayer. Thus, if the time could potentially be extended (as in Sulayman's case), the obligation is established.
The counter-argument could be that this leads to imposing what cannot be done (taklif ma la yutaq), but the response is that it is considered for obligation, not performance.
4
Apply the Derivation to the Case
If her bleeding stops within ten days at the end of the prayer time, and there remains an amount of time sufficient for ghusl and takbir, the prayer is wajib upon her. If not, she is not obligated and must make it up (qada) without sin. This is the mufta bihi position.
Note that the time of ghusl is considered part of the menstruation time, but the takbir time establishes her ability.

Source Text

(٣) قوله: [الزمتها الفريضة] لأنّ وقت الغسل هاهنا من وقت الحيض؛ لأنها لا تعتبر قبله طاهرة عمــــلاً بالتشديد، ووقت التحريمة لإثبات القدرة لها على الفعل، كذا قيل. ١٢
(٤) قوله : [وإلا] أي: وإن لم يبق من الوقت الذي انقطع دمها فيه مقدار ما تغتسل فيه وتحرم للصلاة. ١٢ (5) قوله: [أنه قاء... إلخ] هذا ممّا لم يثبت عند أهل الحديث بل ثبت خلافه في الأحاديث الصحيحة، فمنها ما أخرجه الثلاثة وصححه الترمذي والحاكم عن أبي الدرداء رضي الله عنه مرفوعاً «فَقَاءَ فَتَوَضا»، ومنها ما أخرجه مالك من حديث ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما موقوفاً «كَانَ إِذَا رَعَفَ رَجَعَ فَتَوَضَّأَ»، ومنها ما أخرجه الشافعي رحمه الله وغيره وغيره منه «مَنْ أَصَابَهُ رُعَافٌ أَوْ مَدْيَ أَوقَيْء الصرف فَتَوَضَّأ» و غيرها من الأحاديث المتعدّدة تركناها لخوف الإطناب، وليس للشافعي حجة إلا ما أخرجه الدار قطني عن ثوبان مرفوعاً «قَاءَ فَدَعَانِي بِوَضُوءٍ فَتَوَضَّأَ قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَفَرِيضَةٌ الْوُضُوءُ مِنَ الْقَيْءِ؟ قَالَ: لَوْ كَانَ فَرِيضَةٌ لَوَجَدْتَهُ فِي الْقُرْآنِ» وإسناده واه جداً وليس من الصحيح إلا قصة الأنصاري في نزف الدم، كذا في "الحصول". ١٢

[For] ten days at the end of prayer time, she is obligated for the prayer of that time, even if no time remains from the time; its fruit is qada without sin because she is not negligent at all. 12 the amount to perform ghusl in it. And if her bleeding stops within less than ten days at the end of the time of the menstruating woman. 12 i.e. at that time. 12 i.e. she intends the tahrimah of prayer. 12 prayer if there remains of the time an amount in which she can perform ghusl and say takbir, she is obligated for the prayer. 12 for the invalid prayer according to us, even if it is valid according to others. 12 the prayer is obligatory upon her, otherwise not. (1) His statement: [She is obligated...] because the obligation of the prayer is only lifted from her as a concession for the menstruating woman. So when the menstruation ends, the obligation returns as it was, and the menstruation has ended on the reading that the bleeding stops within ten days, so she is obligated. 12 (2) His statement: [If there remains of the time] The condition of there remaining time enough for ghusl and takbir is because the duty requires ability to perform it, even if that ability is imagined. And it exists here, i.e. at the end of the prayer time, because the time can potentially extend, as was the case for Sulayman (peace be upon him) when the sun stopped when he was shown the swift horses, and he missed the Asr prayer or the litany he had at that time due to preoccupation with them, and he destroyed those horses by slashing and cutting necks as Allah said in His glorious Book: "And he began to pass his hands over the legs and necks" [Sad:33], because they occupied him from the remembrance of his Lord and worship, and he subdued his soul by preventing it from its desires. So Allah rewarded him by returning the sun to its place at the time of prayer so he could make up what he missed of prayer or litany, and He subjected the wind instead of the horses, "running by his command gently wherever he struck." And it cannot be said in this context that considering the imagined ability entails imposing what cannot be done due to the inability to perform the act in that imagined time. The summary of the answer: it was considered for the obligation of performance, not for performance in that time, so understand. 12
(3) His statement: [The prayer is obligatory upon her] because the time of ghusl here is part of the time of menstruation, because she is not considered pure before it, acting on the principle of strictness, and the time of tahrimah is to establish ability for her to act, as it is said. 12
(4) His statement: [otherwise] i.e. if there does not remain from the time in which her bleeding stopped an amount to perform ghusl and say takbir for prayer. 12 (5) His statement: [He vomited... etc.] This is not established among hadith scholars; rather the opposite is established in authentic hadith. Among them is what the three [Imams] narrated and Tirmidhi and Hakim authenticated from Abu Darda (may Allah be pleased with him) marfu'an: "He vomited and performed wudu." Among them is what Malik narrated from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) mauqufan: "When he had a nosebleed, he would go back and perform wudu." Among them is what al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him) and others narrated from him: "Whoever experiences nosebleed or madhi or severe vomit should perform wudu." And other multiple hadith which we left for fear of prolixity. And al-Shafi'i has no proof except what al-Daraqutni narrated from Thawban marfu'an: "He vomited and called for water for wudu and performed wudu. I said: O Messenger of Allah, is wudu obligatory from vomit? He said: If it were obligatory, you would find it in the Quran." Its chain is very weak, and nothing is authentic except the story of the Ansari regarding nosebleed, as mentioned in 'al-Husul'. 12
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a ruling about the obligation of prayer on a menstruating woman when her bleeding stops within ten days at the end of the prayer time. The author explains that if there remains enough time after the bleeding stops to perform ghusl (ritual bath) and to say the takbirat al-ihram (opening takbir), then she is obligated to pray that prayer. If not, she is not obligated. The reasoning is that the obligation of prayer is lifted from a menstruating woman as a concession, so when the bleeding stops, the obligation returns. The condition that time must remain is based on the principle that a person must be capable of performing the required act; here, the ability is considered to exist even if it is only imagined, analogous to the story of Prophet Sulayman (peace be upon him) when the sun was held back so he could make up his missed prayer. The commentary clarifies that this imagined ability is considered for the obligation to perform, not for actual performance in that moment. The passage then transitions to discussing weak arguments, using the example of the hadith about vomiting that the Shafi'i school uses to argue that vomiting does not break wudu. The author refutes this by pointing out that the hadith is not authentic and that authentic hadith prove the opposite. This illustrates how weak arguments (tamasukat da'ifah) are identified and rejected in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الوقت (al-waqt): The time window for a specific prayer.
الغسل (al-ghusl): The ritual bath required to achieve purity after menstruation.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir of prayer that initiates the prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a menstruating woman become obligated to pray after her bleeding stops within ten days?
A) Immediately when the bleeding stops.
B) Only if there remains enough time for ghusl and takbir at the end of the prayer time.
C) If the bleeding stops during the entire prayer time.
D) She is never obligated because she is still impure.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman's prayer obligation is conditional on the remaining time being sufficient for ghusl and takbir, based on the Hanafi principle of imagined ability.

Haram Acts Can Still Produce Legal Effects
Commentary refuting Shafi'i argument on vows to fast on prohibited days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that prohibition does not nullify legal consequences and distinguish this from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Prohibition of an act does not prevent it from having legal effects.

In Hanafi usul, the ruling that an act is haram does not automatically render it legally void. This lesson examines a dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding vows to fast on prohibited days (Eid and Tashreeq), and illustrates the Hanafi position with four case studies. The principle is that legal effects arise from the intrinsic nature of an act, not from its permissibility at a given time.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed issue
The debate is whether a vow to fast on a day that is haram to fast (like Eid) is valid. The Shafi'i school says no; the Hanafi school says yes.
The hadith cited by the Shafi'i is 'Do not fast on these days...'.
2
State the Hanafi position
The vow is valid and must be fulfilled. The prohibition does not invalidate the vow because it arises from an external factor, not from the act of fasting itself.
The Hanafi school distinguishes between the intrinsic ruling of an act and its contingent permissibility.
3
Analyze the opposing proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith's prohibition and the general principle that a vow to commit a sin is invalid.
This is based on the hadith 'No vow in disobedience to Allah'.
4
Examine the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school argues that the prohibition is due to an external cause (being Allah's guest), so the act remains intrinsically valid. The examples in the passage show that haram acts can still produce legal effects.
Examples: ownership via impregnating son's slave-girl, purity via stolen water, etc.
5
Apply the principle to new cases
Generalize the principle: the legal effect (hukm) of an act is not negated by the act being haram due to an external factor.
This is a core Hanafi usul principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تعريف طريق المراد بالنصوص الملك ،وعدمه وكذلك التمسك بقوله عليه السلام: «ألا لا تصوموا في هذه الأيام فإنّها أيام أكل وشرب وبعال» لإثبات أن النذر بصوم يوم النحر لا يصح ضعيف؛ لأن النص يقتضي حرمة الفعل ولا خلاف في كونه حرام وإنما الخلاف في إفادة الأحكام مع كونه حراماً وحرمة الفعل لا تنافي ترتب الأحكام، فإن الأب لو استولد جارية ابنه يكون حراماً ويثبت به الملك، ولو ذبح شاة بسكين مغصوب يكون حراماً ويحل المذبوح، ولو غسل الثوب النجس بماء مغصوب يكون حراماً ويطهر به الثوب، ولو وطىء امرأة في حالة الحيض يكون حراماً ويثبت به إحصان الواطىء ويثبت الحل للزوج الأول.
Section on defining the way of intended meaning from texts. [The issue of] ownership and its absence, and likewise adherence to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Indeed, do not fast on these days, for they are days of eating, drinking, and sexual intercourse' to prove that the vow to fast on the day of Nahr is invalid is weak; because the text indicates the prohibition of the act, and there is no dispute that it is prohibited. Rather, the dispute is in [whether] it produces legal effects while being prohibited, and the prohibition of the act does not preclude the attachment of legal consequences. For if a father impregnates the slave-girl of his son, it is prohibited and ownership is established for him. If he slaughters a sheep with a borrowed knife, it is prohibited and the slaughtered animal is permissible. If he washes a najis garment with stolen water, it is prohibited and the garment becomes purified. If he has intercourse with a woman during menstruation, it is prohibited and the muhsan status of the man is established, and the woman becomes permissible to her first husband.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage is an elaboration of the Hanafi position that an act being haram does not prevent it from having legal consequences. The author begins by refuting the Shafi'i argument that a vow to fast on prohibited days (Eid, Tashreeq) is invalid because the act is haram. The Hanafi respond that the prohibition does not negate the validity of the vow from the perspective of its essence; the prohibition is due to an external factor (not honoring Allah's invitation as guest on those days). The author then provides examples to illustrate that haram acts can produce legal effects: 1) An owner having intercourse with his son's slave-girl is haram, yet it establishes ownership of the offspring for the father. 2) Slaughtering with a borrowed (stolen) knife is haram, yet the meat becomes halal to eat. 3) Washing a garment with stolen water is haram, yet the garment becomes purified. 4) Intercourse during a woman's menstruation is haram, yet it establishes the man's muhsan status (for purposes of zina punishment) and makes the woman permissible to her first husband after divorce. The principle is that the legal effect (hukm) arises from the act itself, not from its permissibility.

Key Terms
حرام (haram): An act that is prohibited by a definitive or probable text, but which can still produce legal consequences.
نذر (nadhr): A vow to perform an act of worship; its validity depends on the act being intrinsically valid, not on being permissible at that time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if someone makes a vow to fast on the day of Eid al-Adha?
A) The vow is invalid because the day is prohibited for fasting.
B) The vow is valid and the person must fast that day.
C) The vow is valid but the person should not fast because it is haram.
D) The vow is invalid and the person must pay kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
Prohibition does not nullify legal consequences; the intrinsic validity of an act is separate from its permissibility at a particular time.

The Principle of Tariq al-Murad: Legal Effects Despite Prohibition
Chapter defining the path to intended meanings from texts with examples of usurped property.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of 'tariq al-murad' to distinguish between the ruling on an act and the ruling on its consequences, using examples from usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
A prohibited means does not nullify the intended legal effect; the law's purpose can be realized despite the prohibition.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi introduces a cornerstone of Hanafi usul: the path to the intended meaning (tariq al-murad) of a text may operate even when the immediate act is forbidden. Through vivid examples—usurped knife, usurped water, and intercourse during menstruation—the author demonstrates that the ruling on the act (hukm taklifi) is distinct from the ruling on its legal effect (hukm wadi'). Understanding this separation is essential for deriving correct rulings and avoiding the error of conflating means and ends.

Guided Path
1
Identify the principle
Recognize that 'tariq al-murad' refers to the method by which the Lawgiver's intended purpose of a text is realized. The passage illustrates that even if the means are forbidden, the purpose (e.g., purification, ownership) can still be achieved.
The principle is not explicitly named in Arabic but is conveyed through examples.
2
Examine each example
For each of the three cases (father taking son's property, slaughter with usurped knife, washing with usurped water, intercourse during menstruation), note the prohibited act and the valid legal effect that follows.
The father's ownership is supported by hadith; the other cases are analogical extensions.
3
Trace the reasoning
Ask: Why does the effect hold despite the prohibition? The answer lies in the intention of the Lawgiver: the prohibition targets the means (e.g., usurpation), while the end (e.g., slaughter, purification) fulfills a different objective that is not inherently corrupt.
This separation is a form of istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas.
4
Connect to the hadith proof
The hadith 'أنت ومالك لأبيك' (You and your wealth belong to your father) is used to establish that the father's taking is valid ownership, even if the son's property is used without explicit permission. This shows that a zanni (speculative) text can still yield a qati (certain) meaning in Hanafi usul.
The thubut is zanni, but the dalala is qati due to the clarity of the wording.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في تعريف طريق المراد بالنصوص
ويثبت به الملك للأب، ولو ذبح شاة بسكين مغصوبة يكون حراما ويحل المذبوح، ولو غسل الثوب النجس بماء مغصوب يكون حراما ويطهر به الثوب، ولو وطىء امرأة في حالة الحيض يكون حراما ويثبت به إحصان الواطىء ويثبت الحل للزوج الأول.
(1) قوله: [ويثبت به الملك] لحديث «أنت ومالك لأبيك» رواه ابن ماجة عن جابر رضي الله تعالى عنه مرفوعاً ورجاله ثقاة، وأخرجه ابن حبان في صحيحه عن عائشة نحوه ورواه البزار وابن عدي في ترجمة سعيد بن بشير عن عمر بن الخطاب رضي الله تعالى عنهما والطبراني وابن عدي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله تعالى عنه بالجملة لا امتراء في صحة متن الحديث.
Chapter on defining the path to intended meanings from texts. And ownership is established for the father. And if one slaughters a sheep with a usurped knife, it is forbidden (haraam) but the slaughtered meat is permissible (halal). And if one washes a najis garment with usurped water, it is forbidden (haraam) but the garment becomes purified by it. And if one has intercourse with a woman during menstruation, it is forbidden (haraam) but it establishes ihsan (protection) for the man and establishes permission for the first husband. (1) His saying: [And ownership is established for the father] based on the hadith: 'You and your wealth belong to your father' narrated by Ibn Majah from Jabir (may Allah be pleased with him) as marfoo', and its narrators are trustworthy; and it was also narrated by Ibn Hibban in his Sahih from Aisha similarly; and it was narrated by al-Bazzar and Ibn Adi in the biography of Sa'id ibn Bashir from Umar ibn al-Khattab (may Allah be pleased with them both); and al-Tabarani and Ibn Adi from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him); in summary, there is no doubt about the authenticity of the text of the hadith.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage from Al-Shashi's Usul al-Fiqh (with commentary) presents a chapter on 'defining the path to intended meanings from texts' (طريق المراد بالنصوص). The author illustrates this principle with three examples involving acts that are forbidden (haraam) due to the use of usurped property or a prohibited act, yet the intended legal effects still occur. First: slaughtering with a usurped knife is forbidden, but the slaughtered animal becomes halal because the prohibition pertains to the misuse of property, not the intrinsic purity of the meat. Second: washing a najis (impure) garment with usurped water is forbidden, but the garment becomes purified because the essence of purification is the removal of najasah, which has been achieved. Third: intercourse during menstruation is forbidden, but it still establishes ihsan (the status of being muhsin for zina penalty) and confirms the permission for the first husband in case of divorce and remarriage. The commentary adds a proof for the first part (ownership established for father) using the hadith 'أنت ومالك لأبيك' (You and your wealth belong to your father), confirming its authenticity. This chapter teaches that in usul, the legal effect does not always depend on the permissibility of the means; rather, the intended meaning of the text (as determined by the Lawgiver) may be realized despite the prohibition.

Key Terms
طريق المراد (tariq al-murad): The path or method by which the intended meaning of a legal text is understood and applied, taking into account that prohibitions may not nullify the underlying purposes.
إحصان (ihsan): In this context, the legal status of being muhsin (protected) for the purpose of the hadd penalty for zina; it is established by valid marriage and intercourse, even if the intercourse is prohibited (e.g., during menstruation).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on the meat of an animal slaughtered with a usurped knife?
A) The meat is haraam because the knife is usurped.
B) The meat is halal because the prohibition is on the use of the knife, not on the slaughter itself.
C) The meat is makruh but permissible.
D) The slaughter is invalid and the meat remains haraam.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a prohibition on the means does not automatically invalidate the end; the intended legal effect may still be realized, as illustrated by the examples of usurped knife, usurped water, and intercourse during menstruation.

The Particle 'في' for Time/Place in Conditional Divorce
Explains the rule for 'في' with time/place

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when 'في' is used for a specific time or place in a divorce statement, it functions as a condition (shart) that suspends the divorce until that time/place occurs.

Core Idea
في للظرف تجعل الطلاق معلقاً بشرط الوقت أو المكان.

This passage from Usul al-Shashi addresses a key linguistic-legal question: how does the particle 'في' affect a divorce statement when it introduces a time or place? The Hanafi school treats this as a conditional suspension, meaning the divorce is not immediate but contingent upon the arrival of that time or place. Understanding this mechanism is crucial for accurate istinbat in divorce-related cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The husband says 'أنت طالق في اليوم' (You are divorced in the day). The ruling is that the divorce is suspended until the day comes.
The condition is a specific future time.
2
Locate the linguistic operation
The word 'في' is used as a zarf (adverb of time/place). In Hanafi usul, this usage is treated as a condition because it links the divorce to a specific future occurrence.
This is based on the literal meaning of 'في'.
3
Trace the reasoning
The condition requires a full day. If the husband says at noon, the day is completed the next day at noon, so the divorce occurs at that time.
The text specifies that half the day counts on the day of swearing and half on the next day.
4
Note the scope
This ruling applies only when 'في' introduces a specific time or place. Other uses, such as with 'في مشيئة الله', have different effects.
The next lesson covers those exceptions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل كلمة في للظرف التي علق الطلاق فيها . ١٢ كتاب للإمام محمد رحمه الله. ١٢ كان في اليوم تطلق حين تجيء من الغد تلك الساعة، وفي "الزيادات " لو قال : أنت طالق في مشيئة الله تعالى أو في إرادة الله تعالى كان ذلك بمعنى الشرط حتى لا تطلق . لأن عدم إدراك وجود الشرط. ۱۲ من الغد؛ (۱) قوله: [ حين تجيء من الغد] يعني: إذا حلف وقت الزوال يقع الطلاق إذا جاء وقت الزوال لأن الشرط معنى يوم كامل، فإذا مضي نصف النهار في يوم الحلف والنصف الثاني من الغد كان اليوم كاملاً فوقع الطلاق لوجود الشرط، كذا في "المعدن". ١٢ (۲) قوله :[لو قال أنت طالق ... إلخ] لأنّه لو قال: «أنت طالق إن شاء الله تعالى» كان ذلك إبطال قولــــه: أنت طالق فكذا ما كان بمعناه، فإن قلت: قوله : «أنت طالق في علم الله» يقع به الطلاق في الحال مع العلم مثل الإرادة في كونهما لا يصلحان ظرفاً؛ لأنهما ،فعلان قيل إنّ العلم يستعمل بمعنى المعلوم، يقال: «اللهم اغفر علمك فينا أي معلومك، ويقال: «علم أبي حنيفة أي: معلومه، وإذا كان بمعـــــى المعلوم يستحيل أن يجعل بمعنى الشرط؛ لأنّ الشرط ما يكون على خطر الوجود ومعلـوم الله تعالى متحقق لا محالة، وإذا كان كذلك كان الطلاق واقعاً في الحال؛ لأنه جعل معلوم الله تعالى ظرفاً للطلاق وإنما يكون الطلاق في معلومه إذا كان واقعاً؛ لأنه لو لم يكن واقعاً لكان عدمه في معلومه بخــــلاف المشية؛ لأنّ مشيئة الله تعالى ليست متحققة حتماً أي وجوباً، وتحقيقه أنّ الله تعالى يوصف بالمشيئة وبضدّها ولا يوصف بضدّ العلم فكان العلم متحققاً لا محالة والمشيئة لا يلزم أن تكون موجودة حتماً، كذا في "الفصول" ، قلت : الأظهر مما قالوا في جواب الاعتراض بقوله : فإن قلت:... إلخ» أن يقال إنه لا حاجة إلى جعل العلم بمعنى العلوم، بل المراد أنه ثابت في علم الله تعالى بمعنى: أن علمه محيط بذلك أي: ما ذكره في "التلويح" إلا أنّ الشارح نقل جواب الأصوليين مع جعل العلم بمعنى المعلوم لورود الاعتراضات على جوابهم بالإرادة والقدرة ليعلم الفرق بين العلم والإرادة والقدرة لوقوع الطلاق في العلم دون الإرادة والقدرة، فافهم. ١٢
Section: The word 'fi' for time/place that suspends divorce. Book of Imam Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him. If he said: 'You are divorced in the day', she will be divorced when that time comes from the next day. In al-Ziyadat: If he said: 'You are divorced in the will of Allah Almighty' or 'in the desire of Allah Almighty', that is in the meaning of a condition, so she is not divorced due to non-realization of the condition. From the next day. His statement: [when that time comes from the next day] means: if he swore at the time of noon, the divorce occurs when the time of noon arrives, because the condition is a complete day. So when half the day passes on the day of swearing and the second half on the next day, the day is complete, so the divorce occurs due to the existence of the condition, as in al-Ma'din. His statement: [If he said 'You are divorced...' etc.] Because if he said: 'You are divorced if Allah wills', that nullifies his statement 'You are divorced', so likewise what is in its meaning. If you say: His statement 'You are divorced in the knowledge of Allah' — divorce occurs immediately by it with knowledge being like desire in that they are not suitable as time/place because they are actions. It is said that 'knowledge' is used in the sense of 'the known'. It is said: 'O Allah, forgive Your knowledge in us' i.e., Your known. And it is said: 'The knowledge of Abu Hanifa' i.e., his known. And when it is in the sense of the known, it is impossible to make it a condition, because a condition is something that is at risk of existence, and the known of Allah Almighty is necessarily existent. And if so, then divorce occurs immediately because he made the known of Allah Almighty a time/place for divorce, and divorce occurs in His known only if it occurs; because if it did not occur, its non-occurrence would be in His known, unlike the will, because the will of Allah Almighty is not necessarily existent necessarily. And its verification is that Allah Almighty is described by will and its opposite, but not described by the opposite of knowledge, so knowledge is necessarily existent, while will is not necessarily existent, as in al-Fusul. I say: The most apparent from what they said in answering the objection by his saying 'If you say...' is that there is no need to make 'knowledge' in the sense of 'the known', but the intended meaning is that it is established in the knowledge of Allah Almighty, meaning that His knowledge encompasses that, as mentioned in al-Talwih, except that the commentator transmitted the answer of the usuliyyun with making knowledge in the sense of the known due to objections arising against their answer concerning desire and power to know the difference between knowledge, desire, and power regarding the occurrence of divorce in knowledge but not in desire and power. So understand.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage from Usul al-Shashi discusses the legal effect of the Arabic particle 'في' (fi) when used in conditional divorce statements. The author, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, clarifies that when 'في' is used for time or place (zarf), it acts as a condition for the divorce. For example, if a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced in the day', she is not divorced immediately but only when that specific time arrives. The condition requires a full day, so if the husband swore at noon, one half of the day passes on that day and the second half on the next day, completing the day, thus divorce occurs. The passage then addresses a more nuanced case: if the husband says 'أنت طالق في مشيئة الله' (You are divorced in the will of Allah) or 'في إرادة الله' (in the desire of Allah), these phrases are treated as conditions meaning 'if Allah wills', so the divorce does not occur because the condition (the will) is not realized as a certainty. In contrast, if he says 'في علم الله' (in the knowledge of Allah), the divorce occurs immediately. The commentary explains the distinction: 'knowledge' (علم) is sometimes used metaphorically to mean 'the known' (معلوم), and since Allah's knowledge encompasses everything, what is known to Him is necessarily existent. Therefore, saying 'in the knowledge of Allah' implies that the divorce is already known to Allah, so it must be occurring now, not conditional. On the other hand, 'will' (مشيئة) can be present or absent, so it functions as a condition that suspends the divorce. The passage also references a response to an objection about why knowledge is not treated like will, and concludes by explaining that the more apparent answer is that there is no need to interpret 'knowledge' as 'the known'; rather, the divorce is simply established in Allah's knowledge, which means it is actual. This lesson is a clear example of how linguistic precision (دلالة الألفاظ) affects legal rulings in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
في (fi): A particle used to indicate time or place, here acts as a condition suspending divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'أنت طالق في اليوم' at noon, when is the divorce effective according to the text?
A) Immediately
B) At noon of the next day
C) At sunset of the same day
D) It never occurs

Key Takeaway
When 'في' introduces a specific time or place in a divorce statement, it creates a condition that suspends the divorce until that time or place arrives.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling

Distinguishing 'في مشيئة الله' and 'في علم الله' in Divorce
Distinguishes rulings for 'في مشيئة الله' and 'في علم الله'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the legal effects of 'في مشيئة الله' and 'في علم الله' in divorce, and explain why the latter causes immediate divorce in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
في علم الله يوجب الطلاق حالاً لأن العلم متحقق لا محالة، بخلاف المشيئة.

This passage continues the discussion of 'في' in divorce statements, now focusing on phrases involving divine attributes. The Hanafi school draws a sharp distinction between 'في مشيئة الله' (in the will of Allah) and 'في علم الله' (in the knowledge of Allah). The former is treated as a condition (like 'if Allah wills'), so the divorce does not occur. The latter, however, triggers immediate divorce because Allah's knowledge is always existent and cannot be uncertain. Understanding this nuanced distinction is critical for accurate fatwa in such cases.

Guided Path
1
State the two phrases and their rulings
If the husband says 'أنت طالق في مشيئة الله', the divorce does not occur. If he says 'أنت طالق في علم الله', the divorce occurs immediately.
The text uses 'في الزيادات' for the first and 'في علم الله' for the second.
2
Identify the reason for the difference
The key is that 'علم' (knowledge) is interpreted as 'المعلوم' (the known), which is necessarily existent. In contrast, 'مشيئة' (will) is not necessarily existent; Allah can will or not will something.
Linguistically, 'علم' is sometimes used to mean 'معلوم'.
3
Understand the objection and answer
An objection arises: why is 'في مشيئة' treated as a condition while 'في علم' is not, even though both are attributes? The answer: Allah is described as having knowledge without opposite, but can be described with will or its opposite. Thus knowledge is certain.
The text also mentions a response without needing to interpret 'علم' as 'المعلوم'.
4
Apply the ruling
In practice, if a husband uses 'في علم الله', the wife is immediately divorced. If he uses 'في مشيئة الله', she remains married unless the condition is met (which effectively never happens because it's tied to divine will).
This distinguishes Hanafi position from other schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary

Key Terms
مشيئة (mashi'ah): Will; here used in 'في مشيئة الله' meaning 'if Allah wills', which nullifies the divorce.
علم ('ilm): Knowledge; in 'في علم الله' it is interpreted as 'the known', causing immediate divorce.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, 'في علم الله' triggers immediate divorce because knowledge is certain, while 'في مشيئة الله' is a condition that prevents divorce.

Khabar al-Wahid and the Classification of Rights
Explains when khabar al-wahid is accepted based on types of legal rights.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify rights into four categories and derive the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid in each, including the disputed ruling on crescent sighting.

Core Idea
Acceptance of a single-narrator report depends on the type of right; hilal testimony requires integrity because the obligation is from the text.

In this lesson, we explore how Hanafi usul classifies legal rights to determine when a single-narrator report (khabar al-wahid) is admissible as proof. The distinction between pure rights of Allah, pure rights of servants, mixed rights, and quasi-testimony governs whether number, integrity, or both are required. We also examine a classical ikhtilaf on the crescent of Ramadan that illustrates the application of these principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four-fold division of rights
The text divides legal rights into four categories: (1) pure rights of Allah (not elaborated here), (2) pure rights of servants involving litigation (financial claims), (3) rights with obligation from one side (mixed), and (4) rights that are one half of testimony (quasi-testimony).
This classification determines the conditions for accepting khabar al-wahid.
2
Derive the condition for each type
For type 2 (financial litigation): both number (two witnesses) and integrity (justice) are required. For type 3 (mixed rights): khabar al-wahid is accepted from both just and sinful reporters. For type 4: either number or integrity suffices, according to Abu Hanifa.
The text cites Qur'an 2:282 and 65:2 for type 2, and analogy (qiyas) for type 4.
3
Analyze the crescent of Ramadan dispute
The text discusses whether the crescent sighting falls under type 3 (mixed) or requires integrity. The correct view (following Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi) is that it requires integrity because the obligation of fasting comes from the text, not the report, making it akin to testimony.
This is a thamarah al-khilaf: a sinful person's report is not accepted for Ramadan.
4
Review the numbered commentary notes
The commentary (from al-Ma'din) elaborates on each point: lawsuits need both for prevention of fraud; transactions without coercion accept any discerning person due to necessity; removal of agent/interdiction require both because they are between pure rights and litigation.
These notes reinforce the classification with examples and rationales.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل خبر الواحد حجة وهو من حقوق العباد ماليس أحد شطريها. أي خصومات المال. و فيه الزام كالوكالات. (1) وأمّا الثاني فيشترط فيه العدد والعدالة ونظيره المنازعات وأمّا الثالث فيقبل أي التعدد وأقله الإثنان. (2) مما يتعامله الناس بلا إلزام. وهو خالص حق العبد ما فيه إلزام من وجه دون وجه فيه خبر الواحد عدلاً كان أو فاسقاً، ونظيرها لمعاملات وأما الرابع أحد شطري الشهادة لأنه لو كان فيه إلزام محض لاشترط كلاهما. فيشترط فيه إما العدد أو العدالة عند أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه ونظيره : العزل والحجر.

بهلال رمضان من النوع الثالث وهو خالص حق العبد ما ليس فيه إلزام؛ لأنّ خبره غير ملزم للصوم بل الملزم هو النص، وأجيب : بأنّ المصنّف عليه الرحمة فيه تابع شمس الأيمة السرخسي عليه الرحمــة، والصحيح ذلك فإن العدالة شرط في الشهادة بهلال رمضان وخبر الفاسق مقبول في النوع الثالث كما سيأتي، كذا في 'المعدن'.

(1) قوله: [المنازعات] كالبيوع والأشربة والأملاك المرسلة بأن ادعى أحد على آخر أنه باع هذا العبد أو اشترى ذلك أو أن ألفاً عليه، فإنه يشترط فيه العدد والعدالة، الأوّل بقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاسْتَشْهِدُواْ شهيدين الآية [البقرة : ۲۸۲] والثاني بقوله عزّ اسمه: وَأَشْهِدُوا ذَوَيْ عَدْلٍ مِّنكُمْ ﴾ [الطلاق : ٢]؛ ولأنّ التزوير والتلبيس والحيل في الخصومات أكثر فشرط زيادة العدد ولفظ الشهادة تقليلاً لها وصيانة للحقوق المعصومة بقدر الوسع والإمكان؛ ولأنّ المنازعة قائمة بين اثنين بخبرين متعارضين من الدعوى وأفكار فلم يقع الفصل والرجحان بجنسه من الخبر بل بخبر ظهرت له مزية على غيره من يمين أو شهادة أي أقوال اثنين أو أكثر، كذا في 'المعدن'.

(2) قوله: [فيقبل فيه خبر الواحد ... إلخ فإنّه عليه السلام كان يقبل الهدية من العادل والفاسق بإخبارهما بأنها هدية؛ ولأنّ الضرورة دعت إلى قبول خبر كلّ مميز ، فإنّ الإنسان قلما يجد المجتمع بشرائط الشهادة كلها ولا دليل للسامع غير هذا الخبر فتسقط الشرائط سوى التميز للضرورة بخلاف خبره عليه السلام، فإنّه لا ضرورة إلى قبول خبر الفاسق ثَمّه لكثرة الرواة العدول وحكم الله تعالى في تلك الحادثة يمكن معرفته بدليل آخر :أي القياس، كذا في 'المعدن'.

(3) قوله: [ونظيره] العزل والحجر :أي: عزل الوكيل وحجر المأذون، فإن فيها إلزاماً من حيث إنّه يلزمهما ألف عن التصرّف و يبطل عملهما في المستقبل وليس بإلزام من حيث إنّ المؤكل والمولى يتصرف في حقه بالفسخ كما يتصرف في حقه بالتوكيل والإذن، فشرطنا فيهما العدد والعدالة لكونهمــا بــين المنزلتين، كذا في 'المعدن'.
A chapter: Khabar al-Wahid is a proof. It is from the rights of the servants that is not one of its two halves, i.e., financial litigations. In it there is obligation like agency agreements. (1) As for the second type, number and integrity are required in it, and its analogy is lawsuits. As for the third type, it is accepted, i.e., multiplicity, and its minimum is two. (2) From what people deal with without obligation. And it is the pure right of the servant in which there is obligation from one aspect and not from another. In it, khabar al-wahid is accepted whether the reporter is just or sinful, and its analogy is transactions. As for the fourth type, it is one of the two halves of testimony because if there was pure obligation, both halves would be required. Therefore, either number or integrity is required in it according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him, and its analogy is removal from office and interdiction. Regarding the crescent of Ramadan, it is from the third type, which is a pure right of the servant that has no obligation, because his report does not oblige fasting; rather, the obligating factor is the text. It was answered that the author, may mercy be upon him, follows Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi, may mercy be upon him, and the correct view is that integrity is a condition for testimony regarding the crescent of Ramadan, and the report of a sinful person is accepted in the third type as will come later. Thus in al-Ma'din. (1) His saying: [Lawsuits] like sales, beverages, and unrestricted properties, wherein one person claims against another that he sold this slave or bought that or that a thousand is owed to him. Number and integrity are required in it. The first by Allah's saying: "And call to witness two witnesses" [al-Baqarah 2:282] and the second by His saying: "And call to witness two just men among you" [al-Talaq 65:2]; and because forgery, deceit, and tricks in lawsuits are more frequent, so increasing the number and the wording of testimony is required to reduce them and protect inviolable rights as much as possible; and because litigation occurs between two parties with two conflicting reports from claim and denial, so the decision and preference are not achieved by the mere type of report but by a report that shows superiority over another through an oath or testimony, i.e., statements of two or more. Thus in al-Ma'din. (2) His saying: [So the report of a single person is accepted... etc.] Indeed, the Prophet, peace be upon him, used to accept gifts from both a just and a sinful person when they informed him that it was a gift; and because necessity calls for accepting the report of every discerning person, for a person rarely finds a group meeting all conditions of testimony, and the listener has no other evidence but this report, so the conditions fall except discernment due to necessity, unlike his report about rights of Allah, peace be upon him, because there is no necessity to accept the report of a sinful person there due to the abundance of just narrators, and the ruling of Allah in that incident can be known through another evidence, i.e., analogy. Thus in al-Ma'din. (3) His saying: [And its analogy] removal from office and interdiction: i.e., removal of an agent and interdiction of a permitted slave, for in them there is obligation in that they are prevented from acting and their future actions are invalidated, but not an obligation in that the principal and master act in their own right by revocation just as they act by authorization and permission, so we required number and integrity in them because they are between the two positions. Thus in al-Ma'din.
Source pages p. 223

Commentary
This passage explains the acceptance of khabar al-wahid (single-narrator report) based on the classification of rights. It divides rights into four categories: (1) Pure rights of Allah, (2) Pure rights of servants, (3) Rights that are partly obligation and partly not, and (4) Rights that are one half of testimony. The type discussed here is about rights of servants. For pure rights of servants involving financial litigation, both number and integrity of witnesses are required. For transactions without obligation, multiplicity (at least two) is required but not necessarily integrity. For rights that involve obligation from one side but not the other, khabar al-wahid is accepted from both just and sinful reporters. For rights that are one half of testimony, either number or integrity is sufficient. The footnote on Ramadan crescent clarifies that according to the correct view, even though it is a pure right of a servant without obligation, integrity is required for testimony. The difference is that the report itself does not oblige fasting; rather, the obligation comes from the text, so the rule is stricter. The commentary also explains that in lawsuits, both number and integrity are required to prevent fraud, supported by Quranic verses. In cases of mutual dealings without coercion, necessity allows accepting reports from any discerning person, even if sinful. The example of removing an agent or interdicting a slave illustrates a mixed right.

Key Terms
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A report narrated by a single person or a number insufficient for tawatur
العدالة (al-adala): Integrity or justice of the witness/reporter, meaning they are upright and trustworthy in religious and moral matters
العدد (al-adad): Number of witnesses, usually a minimum of two for financial claims

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is integrity required for the report of the crescent of Ramadan, even though it is a pure right of the servant?
A) Because the report itself obligates fasting.
B) Because the obligation of fasting comes from the text, making the report a testimony.
C) Because the crescent sighting is classified under financial litigation.
D) Because a minimum of two witnesses is always required for any single-narrator report.

Key Takeaway
The acceptance of khabar al-wahid varies with the type of right; for crescent sighting, the Hanafi school requires integrity because the obligation is ultimately from the text.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
intermediate

Shubha in Hadd: Subject vs Opinion Doubt
Distinguishes two types of shubha and applies to penalty of zina for father and son's slave

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between shubhat al-mahal and shubhat al-zann, and apply the Hanafi rule that textual shubha drops hadd even against personal knowledge.

Core Idea
Textual doubt (shubhat al-mahal) overrides personal knowledge; opinion-based doubt (shubhat al-zann) does not.

In Hanafi usul, the concept of shubha (doubt) plays a critical role in averting fixed punishments (hadd). Not all doubts are equal. This lesson unpacks two fundamental categories: shubha in the subject (arising from a legal text with a prevented effect) and shubha in opinion (based on the individual's mistaken conjecture). Understanding this hierarchy is essential for correctly applying hadd penalties, as demonstrated in the classic case of a father and his son's slave-girl.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of shubha
From the passage, extract the definitions of shubhat al-mahal (textual doubt) and shubhat al-zann (opinion doubt). Note that the former originates from a legal proof (dalil) whose ruling is blocked by a preventer, while the latter stems from the person's own conjecture.
The commentary lists three names: shubhat al-ishtibah, shubhat al-fi'l, and shubhat al-zann for the first type.
2
Understand the basis of strength
The passage argues that shubhat al-mahal is stronger because it is grounded in a text (nass), whereas shubhat al-zann relies on opinion (ra'y). This hierarchy is used to decide whether a person's knowledge of prohibition overrides the doubt.
The principle: 'acting on opinion is less than acting on text.'
3
Apply to the father-son slave example
Consider the scenario: a father has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. Even if he says, 'I knew she was forbidden to me,' the hadd is dropped. This is because a textual shubha exists: the Prophet's hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' creates a doubt about ownership, which is a shubha in the subject (shubhat al-mahal). This doubt is objective and not dependent on the father's belief.
The lineage of the child is also established from the father.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
If shubhat al-mahal were not recognized, the father would be subject to hadd. The Hanafi position drops the punishment, while schools that require subjective doubt might impose it. This illustrates how the classification of shubha directly affects legal outcomes.
The passage also notes that if both parties claim shubha (e.g., the woman says she thought it permissible), hadd is dropped for both due to shared context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعلي اعتبار أن العمل بالرأي دون العمل بالنصّ، قلنا: إنّ الشبهة بالمحلّ أقوى من الشبهة في الظنّ حتى سقط اعتبار ظنّ العبد في الفصل الأوّل ومثاله في ما إذا وطى جارية ابنه لا يحد وان قال: «علمت أنها علي حرام» ويثبت نسب الولد منه لأنّ للأب شبهة الملك له تثبت بالنصّ في مال الابن قال عليه الصلاة والسلام: «أنت ومالك لأبيك». (۱) قوله : [ إن الشبهة بالمحل أقوى ... إلخ] أي: بالفعل وتسمّى شبهة الاشتباه؛ لأنها كانت نشأت من الظنّ، فيكون لها ثلثة أسماء: شبهة الاشتباه وشبهة الفعل وشبهة الظنّ، اعلم أن الشبهة ما يشبه الثابت :أي: الحق وليس بثابت وهي قد تكون شبهة بالفعل وتسمى شبهة اشتباه وهي بالشبهة في الظنّ، وذلك أن يظنّ الإنسان ما ليس بدليل الحل والحرمة دليلاً في كل واحد منهما، وقد تكون شبهة في المحل وتسمّى شبهة الدليل والشبهة الحكميّة وهي أن يوجد الدليل الشرعي النافي للحلّ والحرمة مع تخلّف حكمه لمانع اتصل به فيورث هذا الدليل شبهة في حلّ ما ليس بحلال أو عكسه، وهذا النوع من الشبهة لا يتوقف تحققه على ظنّ الجاني واعتقاده بخلاف القسم الأوّل، فإذا تحقق كلاهما أي كلا الشبهتان فلا بد من أن يكون القسم الثاني من الشبهة في المحل لنشوه عن النص أقوى من الأوّل لاستناده إلى الرأي والظنّ، ولهذا كان الحدّ ساقطاً لشبهة المحلّ وإن كان على خلاف ظنّه فتدبّر، كذا في "المعدن". (۲) قوله: [ومثاله] :أي مثال ما كانت الشبهة في المحل و في الظنّ ومثال سقوط ظنّ العبد فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في المحل وعدم سقوط ظنّه فيما إذا كانت الشبهة في الظنّ، كذا في "المعدن". (۳) قوله: [أنها عليّ حرام] أي: إذا قال الرجل: «إنّها علي حرام»، وقالت جارية الابن: «ظننت أنه يحل لي لايحدّ واحد منهما، أما المرأة فلدعوى الشبهة وأما الرجل فلان الزنا يقوم بهما فإذا سقط الحد عن المرأة سقط عن الرجل مكان الشركة. ١٢
And on the consideration that acting on opinion is less than acting on text, we said: Indeed, shubha (doubt) in the subject (al-mahal) is stronger than shubha in opinion (al-zann), to the extent that the consideration of the individual's opinion falls in the first case. Its example is: when a man has intercourse with his son's slave-girl, he is not subject to the hadd punishment even if he said: 'I knew she was forbidden to me,' and the lineage of the child is established from him because the father has a shubha of ownership proven by text regarding the son's property. The Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'You and your property belong to your father.' (1) His saying: [Indeed, shubha in the subject is stronger... etc.] i.e., in the act, and it is called shubhat al-ishtibah because it arises from opinion. It has three names: shubhat al-ishtibah, shubhat al-fi'l, and shubhat al-zann. Know that shubha is what resembles the established (i.e., truth) but is not established. It may be shubha in the act, also called shubhat ishtibah, which is similar to shubha in opinion, i.e., a person thinks something that is not a proof of permissibility or prohibition is a proof. And it may be shubha in the subject, called shubhat al-dalil and shubha hukmiyya, which is when there is a legal proof negating permissibility or prohibition but its ruling is absent due to a connected preventer, so this proof creates a doubt in the permissibility of what is not permissible or vice versa. This type of shubha does not depend on the perpetrator's opinion and belief, unlike the first type. When both types exist (i.e., both shubhas), the second type (shubha in the subject) must be stronger because it arises from text, while the first relies on opinion and conjecture. Therefore, the hadd punishment is dropped due to shubha in the subject, even if it is contrary to the person's own opinion, so reflect. (2) His saying: [And its example] i.e., an example of where shubha in the subject and in opinion exist, and an example of the fall of the individual's opinion when there is shubha in the subject, and the non-fall of his opinion when there is shubha in opinion. (3) His saying: ['It is forbidden to me'] i.e., if the man says 'She is forbidden to me' and the son's slave-girl says 'I thought it was permissible for me,' then neither is subject to hadd. As for the woman, due to claiming shubha, and as for the man, because zina is established by both, so when hadd is dropped for the woman, it is dropped for the man due to the shared context.
Source pages p. 233

Commentary
This passage is a definition and application of the concept of shubha (doubt/ambiguity) in Hanafi usul, particularly in the context of hadd punishments for zina. The main text argues that shubha in the subject (shubha fi al-mahal) is stronger than shubha in opinion (shubha fi al-zann). The example given is a father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl. Even if the father knew it was forbidden, he is not subject to the hadd punishment because there is a shubha based on textual evidence: the Prophet's hadith 'You and your property belong to your father' creates a legal doubt about ownership, which constitutes shubha in the subject (textual shubha). The commentary expands on the types of shubha: (1) shubhat al-fi'l (act-based, arising from the person's conjecture) and (2) shubhat al-mahal (subject-based, arising from a legal proof, even if the ruling is absent due to a connected preventer). The second type is stronger because it is grounded in textual evidence rather than mere opinion. The hadd is dropped for both the man and the woman in the example if the woman also claimed shubha. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that textual shubha can override apparent guilt and prevent the application of fixed punishments. The passage also notes that when both types of shubha exist, the subject-based shubha prevails.

Key Terms
شبهة المحل (shubhat al-mahal): A doubt arising from a legal proof that normally would indicate something but is prevented from taking effect, creating ambiguity in the subject.
شبهة الظن (shubhat al-zann): A doubt based on the person's own conjecture or mistaken belief about the permissibility of an act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd punishment dropped for the father who has intercourse with his son's slave-girl?
A) Because he thought it was permissible
B) Because the son gave permission
C) Because there is a textual shubha from the hadith 'You and your property belong to your father'
D) Because it was done in private

Key Takeaway
Shubhat al-mahal (textual doubt) is stronger than shubhat al-zann (opinion doubt) and can drop hadd even when the person knows the act is forbidden, as in the father-son slave case.

Al-Hukm al-Shari — The Legal Ruling
